**Trustless First principle.** Any component in which trust in a third party can be eliminated through cryptographic verification is implemented as trustless. Smart contracts execute automatically; votes are recorded on-chain; financial flows pass through auditable contracts. Trust is required only at system boundaries (DUNA legal obligations, interactions with the banking system) and in the bootstrap phase (Founder as initiator).

**Progressive Decentralisation principle.** The architecture is designed so that each component can be decentralised independently of the others. This allows commencement with a partially centralised implementation (BSC instead of GyberNet, GitHub instead of on-chain governance, manual moderation instead of AI) with a sequential transition to full decentralisation as the community grows and technologies mature.

Concrete plan of progressive decentralisation:

```
Component             │ Phase I (Bootstrap)      │ Phase II (Growth)       │ Phase III (Maturity)
──────────────────────┼─────────────────────────┼────────────────────────┼──────────────────────
Blockchain            │ BSC (centralised)        │ BSC + GyberNet testnet  │ GyberNet mainnet
Governance            │ Founder + Safe           │ MacroDAO (delegated)    │ Full DAO autonomy
Data storage          │ Supabase (self-hosted)   │ Supabase + IPFS         │ IPFS + DDP
Frontend              │ DSP Client (hosted)      │ DSP Client + community  │ Federated nodes
AI                    │ External APIs (OpenAI)   │ Fine-tuned + local      │ GyberComputer FL
Moderation            │ Manual + AI flags        │ AI + Social DAO appeal  │ AI + DAO (autonomous)
Finance               │ 80% Governance Pool      │ 50% → Smart contracts   │ 100% DAO-controlled
```

**Compositionality principle.** Each contract implements exactly one function and interacts with others through standardised interfaces (ERC-20, OpenZeppelin Governor, UUPS Proxy). This ensures: (a) auditability — each contract can be verified in isolation; (b) replaceability — any contract can be upgraded through a UUPS proxy without disrupting system operation; (c) testability — 100% coverage of invariants by unit tests and property-based tests (Foundry, Echidna).

**Observability principle.** All significant system states must be observable externally without privileged access. On-chain data is read through public view functions; off-chain metrics are exposed through open APIs and Dune Analytics dashboards. This not only ensures transparency (A2) but also enables the community and AI systems to conduct continuous monitoring of ecosystem health.

#### 4.1.3. Component Interaction: Information Flows

The GyberExperiment architecture is organised as a system of coupled layers, each providing services to the layer above. Information flows between components are formalised as follows:

**Flow 1: Registration and identity (User → DSP → UnitManager)**

```
1. User registers in DSP (email/password → Session)
2. User connects wallet (MetaMask/WalletConnect)
3. DSP sends EIP-712 signature to GPROD
4. GPROD calls UnitManager.registerMember(wallet)
5. On-chain: status = MemberStatus.Unit
6. Supabase: wallet_address recorded as primary key
7. User receives access to full functionality
```

**Flow 2: Project lifecycle (IPI: Idea → Project → Implementation)**

```
1. Participant publishes an Idea in DSP (off-chain, stored in Supabase + IPFS hash)
2. SIC forms organically: other participants join
3. Initiator calls LPBurnInitiator.proposeProject()
4. Social DAO voting: Idea → Project (quorum 5%, 72h)
5. Upon approval: Commerce DAO takes the project into operation
6. G-Plan: tasks, milestone tracking, activity proofs
7. UnitManager.claimReward() — reward for verified activity
8. Upon completion: liquidity pool token/GBR, project token
9. Buyback & burn: 2% of project revenue → GBR burn
```

**Flow 3: Governance (Participant → DAO → Smart Contracts)**

```
1. Participant creates a proposal in DSP
2. AI analyst generates impact analysis
3. Governor.propose() — on-chain record
4. Voting delay: 24–48h (for informing)
5. Voting period: 72h (Social), 120h (Economic)
6. Upon adoption: TimelockController.schedule() — delay 24–48h
7. After timelock: TimelockController.execute() — automatic execution
8. Result recorded on-chain, notifications via DSP
```

**Flow 4: Monitoring and feedback (On-chain → AI → DAO → Correction)**

```
1. On-chain events indexed (The Graph / custom indexer)
2. AI monitoring: analysis of voting patterns, tokenomics, activity
3. Upon anomaly detection: AI generates alert
4. Class "AI recommends": notification to Social DAO
5. Class "AI decides": automatic contract pause (emergency pause)
6. DAO voting: confirmation or cancellation of AI action
7. Result: parameter adaptation (quorum, thresholds, rewards)
```

These four flows form a closed feedback loop: users interact via DSP, their actions are recorded on-chain, AI systems monitor and optimise parameters, DAO adopts corrective decisions that alter the rules of interaction. This is a direct realisation of the CAS model from Section 3.6: agents (users + AI), environment (GyberNet + DSP), rules (smart contracts), feedback loops (monitoring → DAO → correction).

#### 4.1.4. Security Architecture: Defense-in-Depth

The security of CSC is not reducible to the security of individual smart contracts — it is a *systemic property* emerging from the interaction of multiple protective mechanisms at different levels. The present section describes the Defense-in-Depth strategy applied to the GyberExperiment architecture.

**Level 1: Cryptographic.** The foundational security level is provided by the blockchain's cryptographic primitives: ECDSA signatures for transaction authentication, Keccak-256 hashing for integrity, Merkle trees for state verification. At this level, security is determined by mathematical guarantees: breaking ECDSA requires solving the discrete logarithm problem on the elliptic curve secp256k1, which is computationally infeasible at current technological levels (estimate: 2^128 operations).

**Level 2: Smart Contract Security.** The smart contracts UnitManager, Governor, Timelock, GBRVotingWrapper, and LPBurnInitiator are developed using security best practices:

```
Smart Contract Security Stack:

  Patterns:
    — Checks-Effects-Interactions: prevention of reentrancy
    — UUPS Proxy: upgradeability without state loss
    — ReentrancyGuard (OpenZeppelin): explicit protection against
      reentrant calls
    — Pausable: emergency halt capability
    — AccessControl: role-based access model
    — EIP-712: typed signatures for activity proofs

  Audit pipeline (CI/CD):
    1. Slither (static analysis) — detection of known
       vulnerability patterns
    2. Mythril (symbolic execution) — vulnerability discovery
       through formal verification of execution paths
    3. Echidna (fuzzing) — property-based testing
       with randomised inputs
    4. Manual review (peer review via Code DAO process)
    5. External audit (every 6 months or upon major upgrade)

  Post-deployment monitoring:
    — Forta Network: real-time anomaly detection
    — Custom watchers: monitoring of Fund balance,
      unusual voting patterns, mass operations
    — Alert → Emergency multisig → Pause → DAO review
```

**Level 3: Governance Security.** Protection against governance attacks — attacks in which an adversary exploits legitimate DAO mechanisms to cause harm:

- **Flash loan governance attack**: an adversary takes a flash loan to temporarily increase VP. Defence: GBRVotingWrapper requires staking for a minimum period (≥7 days) — VP is available only for locked tokens, rendering flash loans inapplicable.
- **Vote buying**: an adversary purchases votes off-chain. Defence: the square root in Hybrid VP makes buying 51% of VP economically impractical (cost grows exponentially with the target share); voter anonymity at the on-chain level (no on-chain record of individual votes until voting concludes — snapshot voting).
- **Proposal spam**: an adversary clutters governance with meaningless proposals. Defence: minimum threshold for creating a proposal (MemberStatus ≥ Dev(2) + minimum GBR staked); LP Burn for Commerce DAO proposals — an irreversible financial commitment.
- **Governance capture**: gradual accumulation of VP up to DAO control. Defence: Activity Score decay (inactive participants lose VP); qualified majority (≥67%) for critical decisions; Emergency pause for Core (Kill Switch).

**Level 4: Operational security.** Protection of infrastructure (DSP servers, GPROD databases, DDP IPFS nodes):

- TLS 1.3 for all communications;
- Container isolation (Docker) for each module;
- Secret management via HashiCorp Vault or sealed secrets;
- Regular security updates: automated dependency updates via Dependabot/Renovate;
- Incident response plan: severity levels (P0–P3), escalation matrix, post-mortem process.

**Level 5: Economic security.** Protection against economic attacks that exploit market mechanisms to extract value:

- **Oracle manipulation**: protection via Chainlink price feeds (decentralised oracles with economic guarantees);
- **Token price manipulation**: LP Burn creates a "floor price" through irreversibly burned liquidity;
- **Fund exhaustion**: Fund Monitoring + Halving mechanism — automatic reward reduction upon reaching the threshold;
- **Sybil attack**: GNN detector (Appendix F.3) + MemberStatus hierarchy + AI Activity Verifier;
- **MEV (Miner Extractable Value)**: on GyberNet (Phase III+) — private mempool + subsidised gas for DAO operations.

The multi-level security model of CyberSocium differs fundamentally from the approach of most DAOs, which confine themselves to Levels 1–2 (cryptography + contract audits). Levels 3–5 (governance, operational, economic security) are specific to fully-fledged socio-economic systems and reflect the architectural maturity characteristic of CyberSocium.

#### 4.1.5. The Principle of Modular Degradation

A key architectural decision of GyberExperiment is the principle of **modular degradation** (*graceful degradation*): the failure of any individual component does not lead to failure of the system as a whole. The system continues to function with degraded but acceptable performance.

```
Degradation matrix:

  Component failed     | Functions that remain            | Degradation
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  DSP Client           | On-chain: voting, staking,        | No UI;
                       | rewards via direct contract       | participants
                       | interaction (Etherscan/BSCScan)   | use
                       |                                   | CLI/BSCScan
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  GPROD                | DSP Client operates in read-only  | No new
                       | mode (data from cache/IPFS);      | off-chain
                       | on-chain operations available     | operations
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  Supabase (PostgreSQL) | On-chain data available;         | No off-chain
                       | GPROD transitions to read-through | profiles;
                       | from blockchain                   | slowdown
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  AI (all AiC agents)  | Manual Activity Score;            | Slower
                       | manual moderation; proposals      | processing;
                       | without summarisation             | increased
                       |                                   | participant load
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  BSC (blockchain)     | STOP: core functions (token,      | Critical
                       | voting, rewards) unavailable      | failure; plan:
                       | Mitigation: migration to backup   | transition to
                       | RPC endpoint; Phase III+:         | GyberNet
                       | GyberNet as alternative           |
  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼──────────────
  DDP (IPFS)           | Data accessible via               | Central
                       | centralised fallback (S3);        | fallback;
                       | violation of A1, but availability | temporary
                       | preserved                         | centralisation

  Single point of failure: the blockchain itself (BSC in Phases I–II).
  Mitigation: BSC health monitoring + plan B (GyberNet, Phase III).
```

This principle follows from Axiom A4 (extensibility): the system must be capable of adapting to environmental changes, including component failures. The modular architecture (DSP Client ↔ GPROD ↔ CONTRACTS ↔ Supabase ↔ DDP) ensures that each module can be replaced, upgraded, or deactivated without cascading failure. This is a direct realisation of Ashby's Law (Section 2.4.1): the variety of protective mechanisms must match the variety of threats.

### 4.2. GyberCommunityToken (GBR): Tokenomics

#### 4.2.1. Token Specification

```
Name:               GyberCommunityToken
Ticker:             GBR
Standard:           BEP-20 (Binance Smart Chain)
Contract address:   0xa970cae9fa1d7cca913b7c19df45bf33d55384a9
Type:               Utility Token
Total supply:       Fixed (determined at contract deployment)
Additional
issuance:           Impossible (contract contains no mint function
                    after initialisation)
```

**Token functions within the ecosystem:**

```
1. Governance:
   — Voting in DAO (Social, Code, Commerce, Economic)
   — Signing proposals
   — Condition: wallet must be active
     (verified by a dedicated algorithm at voting time)

2. Work evaluation:
   — Means of evaluating participant contributions to projects
   — Reward via UnitManager
     (proportional to status and verified activity)

3. Infrastructure interaction:
   — Interaction with GyberNet Blockchain
   — Interaction with GyberComputer
   — Confirmation of seriousness of intent when initiating projects
     (burning 0.1% of C(p) upon transition to Accumulation)

4. Staking:
   — GBR staking: staking rate determined by Economic DAO vote
     and adapted to the economic parameters of the ecosystem
   — Enhancement of participant reputation
   — Passive income

5. Medium of exchange:
   — Trading on DEX (PancakeSwap)
   — Interaction with project liquidity pools
   — Discounts for special project clients
```

#### 4.2.2. Emission Distribution and Governance

```
Distribution (fixed supply, deflationary model):

  Governance Pool (~80%+):
— Controlled by initiators and key community
  participants at the deployment stage
  of the experiment
— Used for on-chain voting, UnitManager financing,
  and reserve operations
— As the system becomes automated, funds are transferred
  to a stabilisation fund — a smart contract
  governed exclusively through DAO voting
— Managed via the BEP-20 delegation mechanism

  Trading Float (~20% or less):
— Listed on DEX (PancakeSwap)
  for liquidity provision and price discovery
— Creates a market mechanism for determining
  the value of GBR
```

#### 4.2.3. Reward Mechanism: UnitManager

UnitManager is a smart contract implementing the RewardProtocol and constituting the technical realisation of Axiom 5 (meritocratic fairness).

**Implementation status:** the current version of UnitManager (GybernatyUnitManager) is a working prototype demonstrating the principle of automatic reward distribution based on participant status. The prototype implements four levels (Unit, Dev, LeadDev, ArchDev), a two-level approval system (confirmation by participants one and two levels higher), and restrictions on withdrawal frequency (up to 2 times per month). Integration with G-Plan for activity verification is the next development stage.

**Reward payment algorithm:**

```
1. Fixed reward per Unit Type:
   Each participant receives a fixed amount
   determined by their status (Unit Type):

   — Unit (level 1):    10,000,000 GBR / period
   — Dev (level 2):     100,000,000 GBR / period
   — LeadDev (level 3): 1,000,000,000 GBR / period
   — ArchDev (level 4): 10,000,000,000 GBR / period

   The reward is paid for verified activity
   in the current period.

2. Project completion bonus (×5 multiplier):
   Upon verified completion of a project in the IPI model
   (transition to the Operation phase), all members
   of the project team receive a bonus:

   reward_completion(aᵢ) = reward_base(statusᵢ) × 5

   The ×5 multiplier creates a colossal economic
   incentive to complete what was started: a team
   that brings a project to Operation earns in a single
   period as much as in five ordinary periods. This resolves
   the systemic problem of incomplete projects —
   a blight on both open-source communities and
   corporate innovation programmes.

3. Activity verification:
   UnitManager queries G-Plan — an innovative
   task manager developed by the community.

   G-Plan verifies activity aᵢ by checking:
   — Participation in tasks during the reporting period
   — Task completion confirmed by participants
     of higher status
   — Overall level of engagement in ecosystem projects

4. Payment:
   If activity confirmed:
     UnitManager.transfer(walletᵢ, reward_amount)
   If project completed:
     UnitManager.transfer(walletᵢ, reward_amount × 5)
   If activity not confirmed:
     Transaction rejected. Participant may
     retry after accumulating activity.

5. Record:
   All operations are recorded on the BSC blockchain,
   ensuring full transparency and auditability.
```

**Connection to theory.** UnitManager realises several axioms simultaneously:
- A2 (transparency): all payments are on-chain, verifiable by anyone
- A5 (meritocracy): reward is determined by status and activity, not capital
- A6 (inclusivity): minimum status (Unit) is accessible to every active participant

**Free-riding countermeasure:** reward is paid not for "presence in the system" but for verifiable completion of specific tasks in G-Plan. The ×5 multiplier for project completion creates an additional incentive for genuine contribution rather than minimal simulation of activity. AI verification of task quality (Section 6.4) provides a primary filter against formal completion without substantive output.

Critical distinction from existing DAOs: in most DAOs, rewards are determined by token-holder or administrator voting — creating subjectivity and politicisation. In UnitManager, rewards are determined by **objectively verifiable activity** through G-Plan, and the amount is tied to status determined by the community. This minimises the space for manipulation.

#### 4.2.4. Liquidity Pools and Connection to Projects

The liquidity pool mechanism is a key element in the realisation of Axiom 6 (inclusivity) and Loop 2 (liquidity):

```
For each project pⱼ transitioning to the Operation state:

1. Internal project tokens token(pⱼ) are issued
   (at the Accumulation stage, for sale at 1 BUSD)

2. Before opening trading on DEX, a liquidity pool is created:
   Pool(pⱼ) = {token(pⱼ), GBR}

3. This means token(pⱼ) trades in a pair with GBR

4. Consequences for participants:
   — Any GBR holder may acquire token(pⱼ)
     via DEX, regardless of participation in SIC(pⱼ)
   — Active participants receiving GBR through UnitManager
     automatically have access to the tokens of any project
   — This realises the principle: "active community members
     receive tokens of any project, regardless of
     personal participation in that specific project"

5. Staking of internal tokens:
   token(pⱼ) staking: 10 / [total_supply(token(pⱼ))] %
   of the revenue of project pⱼ

   This creates a direct economic link between
   the success of a project and the reward of
   its token holders.

6. Project client tiers:
   — External clients: use fiat currency,
     pay full price
   — Special clients: use GBR,
     receive a discount
   — Super-clients: use token(pⱼ),
     receive maximum discount

   This creates an economic incentive for acquiring
   and holding GBR and token(pⱼ), supporting
   token liquidity and value.
```

To prevent liquidity fragmentation at ecosystem scale, minimum liquidity thresholds for each pool are prescribed, determined by Commerce DAO voting, as well as an aggregation mechanism through PowerSwapMeta (Section 6.5).

#### 4.2.5. Liquidity Pool: Architecture and Management

GBR liquidity is provided through DEX pools on PancakeSwap with a dual trading pair. The liquidity architecture is designed to ensure stable price discovery and market depth.

```
Liquidity parameters:

  DEX:              PancakeSwap v2 (migration to v3 via
                    governance vote upon reaching maturity)
  Trading pairs:    GBR/BNB (50% of liquidity) +
                    GBR/USDT (50% of liquidity)
  LP provider:      Exclusively DUNA — the sole
                    provider of base liquidity
  Locked Liquidity: Team.Finance, locked for 12 months
                    with extension via governance vote
  Initial capital:  $50,000–100,000 from DUNA treasury
                    (approved by governance vote)

Rationale for 50/50 split:
  GBR/BNB (50%):   Primary trading pair for
                   BSC users, high volumes
  GBR/USDT (50%):  Stable USD price discovery,
                   simplifies buyback & burn,
                   lower Impermanent Loss

"DUNA only as LP" model:
  — Full community control over liquidity
    through governance
  — All trading fees (0.25% on v2) go to
    DUNA treasury
  — Guaranteed market depth, independent
    of the discretion of individual LP providers
  — Transparency: all liquidity visible on-chain,
    managed through Timelock
  — LP tokens locked via Team.Finance for
    12 months → public page with countdown timer
    to confirm rug pull protection
```

#### 4.2.6. LP Burn Mechanism: Proof-of-Commitment for Project Initiation

LP Burn is a unique economic mechanism with no direct analogues in the existing DAO ecosystem. It solves the problem of filtering serious proposals from spam, while simultaneously deepening ecosystem liquidity.

**Operating principle.** A participant wishing to initiate a new project, research effort, or critical vote creates their own LP position (GBR + BNB/USDT) on PancakeSwap and *burns* the resulting LP tokens through a dedicated Gybernaty smart contract. Burning LP tokens is an irreversible financial commitment (proof-of-commitment), after which the participant receives the right to initiate:
- A new research project via Commerce DAO or Economic DAO
- A product development proposal
- A critical governance vote (when GBR is insufficient for the Proposal Threshold)

```
LP Burn economics:

  Procedure:
    1. Participant creates an LP position (GBR + BNB/USDT)
       on PancakeSwap
    2. Receives LP tokens (CAKE-LP)
    3. Burns LP tokens via the LPBurnInitiator contract
    4. Contract verifies minimum threshold
       ($1,000–$5,000, determined by governance)
    5. Participant receives the right to initiate

  Why burn, not stake:
    — LP burn = irreversible commitment
      (cannot be recovered → not speculation, but conviction)
    — Double stake: participant deposits both GBR
      and BNB/USDT simultaneously
    — Upon burn, liquidity remains in the pool permanently →
      market depth increase → benefit for the entire ecosystem
    — If proposal rejected: the burner lost funds,
      but deepened liquidity for all → no
      "free spam"

  Example:
    Participant wishes to launch a research project
    on swarm intelligence algorithms:
    1. Creates an LP position for $5,000 (GBR + BNB)
    2. Burns LP tokens via the contract
    3. Submits a proposal for a $30,000 grant from DUNA
    4. Community votes:
       Approved → participant receives the grant
       Rejected → participant lost $5,000,
       but ecosystem liquidity increased

  Protection against abuse:
    — Minimum LP burn threshold ($1,000–$5,000)
    — Limit on the number of LP burn proposals per month
      (determined by governance)
    — Whitelist for participants with a history of successful
      projects (exemption from LP burn)

  Implementation status: contracts implemented
  and in the testing phase
```

**Theoretical justification.** LP Burn realises the principle of *costly signalling* from evolutionary biology (Zahavi, 1975): a costly signal (irreversible burning of funds) is a reliable indicator of seriousness of intent, since it cannot be falsified. In mechanism design theory, this corresponds to the *screening* principle (Rothschild & Stiglitz, 1976): the mechanism separates agents with high and low motivation through self-selection, without requiring centralised evaluation.

#### 4.2.7. Deflationary Model and Buyback & Burn

GBR tokenomics is built on a deflationary model: the total supply decreases monotonically through several burning mechanisms.

```
GBR burning mechanisms:

  1. Buyback & Burn (operational):
     — DUNA directs a portion of ecosystem revenues
       (LP trading fees, project revenues)
       toward buyback of GBR from the DEX
     — Purchased tokens are burned
       (transfer to 0x000...dead)
     — Legal characterisation: "protocol liquidity
       management operation"
       (asset management operation),
       NOT profit distribution
     — Effect: at stable demand — growth in
       GBR value → growth in real value of
       UnitManager rewards

  2. LP Burn (initiatory):
     — Participants burn LP tokens upon initiating
       projects (Section 4.2.6)
     — Effect: liquidity remains in the pool permanently,
       but the burner's LP share disappears

  3. Project Initiation Burn:
     — Burning of 0.1% of C(p) upon project
       transition to the Accumulation phase
     — Confirmation of seriousness of intent +
       deflationary pressure

  4. Activity Scoring Penalties:
     — Penalties for inactivity (burning of a portion
       of staked GBR when Activity Score falls
       below the threshold)

  Aggregate deflationary effect:
    total_supply(t+1) = total_supply(t)
      — buyback_burn(t)
      — lp_burn(t)
      — initiation_burn(t)
      — penalty_burn(t)

  As the ecosystem grows, all four components grow →
  accelerating deflation → increase in GBR value
  with growing demand (new participants, new projects)
```

**Protection against classification as a security (Howey Test).** Buyback & Burn does not constitute profit distribution among participants. The DUNA Association Agreement explicitly states: "GBR tokens do NOT entitle holders to dividends or profit distributions". Buyback & Burn is formalised as an "asset management operation to maintain protocol liquidity" — analogous to a corporation buying back its own shares from the market without any obligation to pay dividends. A detailed Howey Test analysis is provided in Section 8.4.2.

#### 4.2.8. Economic Equilibrium and Tokenomics Sustainability

GBR tokenomics is designed to achieve long-term equilibrium between emission (UnitManager rewards) and deflation (four burning mechanisms). We formalise the conditions of this equilibrium.

**Flow balance model:**

Let S(t) denote the circulating supply of GBR at time t. The dynamics of S(t) are determined by:

```
dS/dt = emission(t) - burn(t)

where:
  emission(t) = Σ_status reward(status) × N_active(status, t)
  — aggregate reward to all active participants by status

  burn(t) = buyback_burn(t) + lp_burn(t) + initiation_burn(t) + penalty_burn(t)
  — aggregate burning from all sources
```

**Three regimes:**

1. **Inflationary regime (dS/dt > 0):** emission > burn. Characteristic of early phases, when the ecosystem distributes rewards to attract participants but has not yet generated sufficient revenue for buyback & burn. In this regime, the GBR price experiences downward pressure, offset by growing utility (voting, staking, access to services).

2. **Equilibrium regime (dS/dt ≈ 0):** emission ≈ burn. The target state of a mature ecosystem. Circulating supply stabilises; the GBR price is determined by the balance of supply and demand at the utility value level.

3. **Deflationary regime (dS/dt < 0):** burn > emission. Characteristic of a mature ecosystem with multiple revenue-generating projects. Buyback & burn from project revenues exceeds the emission of new tokens. In this regime, circulating supply contracts, creating upward price pressure at stable or growing demand.

**Parameter estimates for three phases:**

| Parameter | Phase I (Bootstrap) | Phase II (Growth) | Phase III+ (Maturity) |
|---|---|---|---|
| N_active | 50–500 | 500–5,000 | 5,000–100,000+ |
| Monthly emission | ~10B GBR | ~50B GBR | ~100B GBR |
| Project revenues (monthly) | $0 | $1K–$50K | $50K–$5M |
| Buyback & burn (monthly) | 0 GBR | ~1B GBR | ~50B–200B GBR |
| LP burn (monthly) | ~0.1B GBR | ~1B GBR | ~5B GBR |
| Regime | Inflationary | Transitional | Deflationary |

**Halving formula:**

To prevent exhaustion of the reward fund (60% of total supply = 6T GBR), a halving mechanism is provided — an automatic reduction of rewards upon reaching threshold levels:

```
reward_multiplier(t) = {
  1.0,   if remaining_fund > 50% of initial_fund
  0.75,  if remaining_fund ∈ (25%, 50%] of initial_fund
  0.50,  if remaining_fund ∈ (10%, 25%] of initial_fund
  0.25,  if remaining_fund ≤ 10% of initial_fund
}

actual_reward(status, t) = base_reward(status) × reward_multiplier(t) × activity_multiplier(i)
```

Halving ensures that the reward fund is never fully exhausted (asymptotic approach to zero), while rewards remain meaningful over decades (provided GBR price growth compensates for halving in real terms).

**FundMonitor contract:**

Automated monitoring of the reward fund state is implemented through the FundMonitor smart contract:

```solidity
// FundMonitor pseudocode
contract FundMonitor {
    uint256 public constant INITIAL_FUND = 6_000_000_000_000; // 6T GBR
    uint256 public remainingFund;

    function getMultiplier() public view returns (uint256) {
        uint256 ratio = (remainingFund * 100) / INITIAL_FUND;
        if (ratio > 50) return 100; // 1.0x
        if (ratio > 25) return 75;  // 0.75x
        if (ratio > 10) return 50;  // 0.50x
        return 25;                   // 0.25x
    }

    function monthlyReport() external returns (
        uint256 remaining,
        uint256 monthlyEmission,
        uint256 projectedRunway
    ) {
        // Publishes an on-chain report on fund status
        // projectedRunway = remaining / monthlyEmission in months
    }
}
```

**Stress-testing (cadCAD scenarios):**

Prior to launch, Economic DAO will conduct cadCAD modelling of the following stress scenarios:

1. **Rapid growth:** 10× participants in 6 months. Test: does reward fund sustain emission? Expectation: halving activates, but real value of rewards grows through increased GBR utility.

2. **Price crash:** GBR loses 90% of value in one week. Test: death spiral or recovery? Expectation: fixed supply + buyback from stabilisation fund + preservation of utility → recovery.

3. **Mass sell-off:** 30% of stakers withdraw funds. Test: does LP liquidity hold? Expectation: LP burn ensures permanent liquidity; sell-off creates price pressure but does not destroy liquidity.

4. **Regulatory shock:** GBR is delisted from PancakeSwap. Test: does the ecosystem continue to function? Expectation: migration to alternative DEXs (SushiSwap, 1inch); GBR utility within the ecosystem is independent of external DEXs.

**Target equilibrium parameters (Phase III):**

```
  Circulating supply:       ~7–8T GBR (accounting for emission + burn)
  Velocity:                 ~4–6 turnovers per year (comparable to ETH)
  Staked ratio:             30–50% of circulating supply
  TVL (all pools):          ≥$10M
  Gini (GBR distribution):  < 0.5
  Active participation rate: ≥30% of registered participants
  Revenue/market_cap ratio: ≥5% (indicates genuine utility value rather than speculation)
```

### 4.3. Decentralised Social Platform (DSP): Architecture

#### 4.3.1. Overview and Principles

DSP (Decentralised Social Platform) is a social platform owned by all users and governed by them through DAO. DSP is not merely a communication tool but the **operating system of CSC** — the environment in which the entire project lifecycle (IPI) takes place, SICs form, AGs operate, G-Plan functions, and the day-to-day interaction of participants occurs.

**Architectural principles (derived from axioms):**

```
From A1 (decentralisation):
  — DSP is a network of nodes, not
    a client-server application
  — Each node contains a set of microservice containers
  — No single point of failure
  — Each participant may deploy their own node

From A3 (data sovereignty):
  — Three levels of data protection:
    Level 1 (basic): server-side encryption
      using the client's public key
    Level 2 (enhanced): client-side encryption
      prior to transmission to the server
    Level 3 (maximum): full end-to-end
      encryption; the server stores only encrypted
      data; keys held exclusively by the user
  — Even the basic level provides optimal protection
  — The user has 100% control over their data

From A4 (extensibility):
  — Modular architecture: each user may write
    their own code module
  — A module can be included in a node and offered
    to other participants
  — Each node can be supplemented with any
    existing or new modules
  — Extensibility via GitHub repository
  — The system expands in all directions

From A7 (self-governance):
  — The state of the platform's codebase is determined
    by the main branch of the GitHub repository
  — Changes to the main branch are made
    only through Code DAO voting
  — Any participant may propose a change
    (pull request), but adoption is through DAO

From A8 (cognitive augmentation):
  — AI content moderation: a language model
    trained on community rules classifies
    content in real time. The model's decisions
    are advisory — the final decision
    is made by Social DAO participants.
    Formally: flag(m) = LLM(m, Rules_DAO) ∈ {ok, review, reject},
    where review → queue for human moderators
  — AI recommendations: a system for recommending projects,
    tasks, and SICs based on the participant's
    competency profile. The model runs locally (on-device);
    raw data does not leave the device (A3)
  — AI participant assistant: a contextual assistant
    for navigating the ecosystem — explaining
    DAO mechanics, assisting in drafting proposals,
    summarising discussions. Operates as an interface
    to documentation and on-chain data, without access
    to users' private data
```

#### 4.3.2. DSP Technology Stack

The choice of technology stack for DSP is determined by a trade-off between technological maturity (minimising bootstrap-phase risks), compatibility with blockchain infrastructure, and readiness for progressive decentralisation.

**Frontend (DSP Client — client-side component of DSP):**

- **Framework:** Next.js 15 (React 19, App Router, Server Components)
- **Rationale:** server components provide SEO and initial-load performance; the React ecosystem offers the largest developer pool for open-source contribution; App Router provides type-safe routing
- **Web3 integration:** wagmi + viem for interaction with BSC/GyberNet; RainbowKit for wallet connection (MetaMask, WalletConnect, Coinbase Wallet)
- **Real-time:** WebSocket (Socket.IO) for chat and notifications; Server-Sent Events for DAO voting updates
- **Localisation:** i18next with support for Russian and English as a minimum; the architecture allows addition of arbitrary locales

**Backend (GPROD — Gyber Production Backend):**

- **Framework:** NestJS 11 (TypeScript, ESM modules)
- **Role:** blockchain middleware — not a full-featured backend, but a linking layer between DSP and on-chain infrastructure
- **ORM:** Prisma 6 with PostgreSQL (Supabase self-hosted)
- **Key functions:** EIP-712 signature verification; on-chain event indexing; blockchain data caching; API for DSP
- **Authentication:** two-level model: (1) password session → restricted access; (2) wallet connection → full access to Web3 functionality

**Database:**

- **Supabase (self-hosted PostgreSQL):** primary off-chain data store (profiles, projects, G-Plan tasks, metadata)
- **Wallet Address = primary key:** all tables are linked via wallet_address, providing unified identity across modules
- **Row Level Security (RLS):** native Supabase support ensures A3 (data sovereignty) at the database level
- **Realtime:** built-in Supabase Realtime for push notifications on data changes

**Distributed storage (DDP — Distributed Data Protocol, Phase 2):**

- **IPFS:** content-addressed storage for documents, media files, voting hashes
- **Content Registry (smart contract):** on-chain registry of CIDs (Content Identifiers), ensuring immutability of references
- **ACL (Access Control List):** cryptographic access control: public, SIC-only, personal-only
- **Community Pinning Nodes:** community participants provide storage in exchange for GBR rewards

#### 4.3.3. Data Model and Identity

The central concept of DSP is the **wallet as a unified identity**. Instead of the traditional model (email/password → internal ID → relations), DSP uses the cryptographic wallet address as the root identifier:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              Wallet Address (PK)             │
│    0xa1b2c3d4e5f6...                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ On-chain:                                    │
│   MemberStatus (UnitManager)                │
│   GBR Balance (ERC-20)                      │
│   Voting Power (GBRVotingWrapper)           │
│   Activity Proofs (EIP-712 signed)          │
│   Staking Position                           │
│   Soulbound Tokens (audit, reputation)      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Off-chain (Supabase):                        │
│   Profile (name, avatar, bio, skills)       │
│   Projects (created, participated)          │
│   G-Plan Tasks (assigned, completed)        │
│   Social Graph (connections, SIC membership)│
│   Preferences (language, notifications)     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Distributed (IPFS/DDP):                      │
│   Personal Documents                         │
│   Published Content                          │
│   Encrypted Messages                         │
│   Portfolio & Credentials                    │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**DID (Decentralized Identifier):** in Phase II, each participant receives a DID in the format `did:gybernaty:<wallet_address>`, linked to an on-chain record in UnitManager. A DID enables: (a) cross-platform identification; (b) issuance and verification of Verifiable Credentials (VC); (c) identity portability — a participant may transfer their identity to any DSP-compatible node.

**Verifiable Credentials (VC):** documents signed with the digital signature of the issuing party (DAO, another participant, AI auditor), confirming specific attributes: status in UnitManager, project participation, AI audit results, qualifications. VCs are stored by the participant (self-sovereign) and presented on demand without reference to a central registry.

### 4.4. GyberNet: Community Blockchain

GyberNet is a specialised community blockchain serving as the *trust layer* for the entire GyberExperiment ecosystem. GyberNet is a direct realisation of Axioms A1 (decentralisation) and A2 (transparency) at the infrastructure level.

#### 4.4.1. Purpose and Functional Profile

Unlike general-purpose blockchains (Ethereum, BSC), GyberNet is designed as a **specialised blockchain for CSC** — optimised for a specific set of operations:

- **Recording DAO decisions:** every vote, every proposal, every decision execution is recorded immutably. This ensures full auditability of governance — any participant may at any time verify the entire history of decisions
- **Registering statuses and activity:** changes to MemberStatus (Unit → Dev → LeadDev → ArchDev → Core), activity proofs (EIP-712 signatures), G-Plan records — all significant ecosystem state changes are recorded on-chain
- **Document hashing:** all critical documents (proposals, reports, audit results) are hashed and recorded on-chain, providing proof of existence and immutability without storing the documents themselves in the blockchain
- **Financial flows:** all GBR transactions, LP operations, staking, buyback & burn — transparent and verifiable
- **Identity:** DID registry, Verifiable Credentials anchor, soulbound tokens

#### 4.4.2. Current Implementation: BSC as a Transitional Platform

In the initial stage (Phases I–II), GyberNet functions are fulfilled through BNB Smart Chain (BSC). The choice of BSC is motivated by:

| Parameter | BSC | Ethereum L1 | Polygon | Solana |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Fee | ~$0.01–0.03 | ~$5–50 | ~$0.01 | ~$0.001 |
| Block time | ~3 sec | ~12 sec | ~2 sec | ~0.4 sec |
| EVM compatibility | Full | Native | Full | None |
| DeFi infrastructure | Mature (PancakeSwap) | Maximum | Mature | Mature |
| Stability | High (>3 years without downtime) | Maximum | High | Medium (historical outages) |
| Validator centralisation | Medium (21 validators) | Low (>500k) | Medium (100+) | Low (1500+) |

BSC provides an optimal balance between cost, speed, and infrastructure for the bootstrap phase. The centralisation of BSC validators (21 nodes) is a deliberate compromise: in the initial stage, the priority is functionality and accessibility, not maximum decentralisation. Migration to GyberNet mainnet (Phase III) will eliminate this limitation.

#### 4.4.3. Prospective Architecture of GyberNet

GyberNet is designed as an **application-specific blockchain** with a five-layer architecture:

**Layer 1 — Consensus (Reputational Proof-of-Stake, RPoS):**

A modified PoS in which validator weight is determined not only by the quantity staked but also by reputation within the ecosystem:

```
validator_weight(v) = √(staked_GBR(v)) × (1 + ActivityScore(v) / 100)
```

Where ActivityScore is the aggregated activity score of the validator, computed from G-Plan data, voting participation, and Code DAO contributions. The square root of staking reduces the weight of large holders (anti-plutocratic mechanism), while the reputational multiplier incentivises genuine ecosystem participation.

Consensus parameters:
- Minimum validator stake: 100,000 GBR (calibrable through Economic DAO)
- Validator set size: 50–200 (grows with the ecosystem)
- Epoch length: 100 blocks (~5 minutes)
- Slashing conditions: double signing (100% slash), offline >24h (1% slash per day), malicious proposals (50% slash + status reduction)
- Block leader rotation: weighted random selection proportional to validator_weight

**Layer 2 — Execution (EVM-compatible):**

Full compatibility with the Ethereum Virtual Machine for reuse of all existing contracts without modification. Additional precompiled contracts for CSC-specific operations:
- `0x0100` — ActivityProof verification (native EIP-712 activity proof verification)
- `0x0101` — ReputationQuery (reading Activity Score without external call)
- `0x0102` — DAOStatus (fast query of voting status)

**Layer 3 — Storage (State + History):**

Separation into "hot" (active state: balances, statuses, current votes) and "cold" (archival: completed votes, historical activity proofs) storage. Hot storage is optimised for fast access; cold storage for long-term retention with Merkle proofs of integrity.

**Layer 4 — Network (P2P + Cross-chain):**

LibP2P for peer discovery and transaction propagation. Cross-chain bridge with BSC and Ethereum: lock-mint scheme with M-of-N threshold signatures (not a centralised relayer). The bridge is governed by Economic DAO — adding new chains requires a vote.

**Layer 5 — API and indexing:**

Built-in JSON-RPC API (Ethereum-compatible), The Graph protocol for event indexing, WebSocket API for real-time subscriptions. All APIs are public and free of charge (A2).

### 4.5. GyberComputer: Distributed Computing

GyberComputer is a private distributed computing network of the community, providing computational resources for the GyberExperiment ecosystem without dependence on centralised cloud providers (AWS, GCP, Azure).

#### 4.5.1. Purpose and Economic Model

GyberComputer realises Axiom A1 (decentralisation) in the domain of computational infrastructure. Its purposes are:

- **DSP node hosting:** ensuring fault tolerance of the social platform without dependence on a single provider
- **AI model training and inference (AiC project):** distributed training through Federated Learning, local inference to ensure A3 (data sovereignty)
- **IPFS content pinning:** ensuring availability of ecosystem files through a distributed storage network
- **Computationally intensive tasks:** cadCAD simulations, cryptographic proofs, off-chain batch data processing

**Economic model:**

Participants providing computational resources (CPU, GPU, RAM, storage) receive GBR rewards according to the formula:

```
reward(node, epoch) = base_reward × resource_utilization(node) × uptime_multiplier(node) × quality_score(node)
```

Where:
- `base_reward` — base rate per epoch, determined by Economic DAO
- `resource_utilization` — fraction of resources utilised (0..1)
- `uptime_multiplier` — multiplier for availability time (0.5 at uptime <90%, 1.0 at >99%)
- `quality_score` — quality rating: response speed, computation correctness, absence of downtime (0.5..1.5)

#### 4.5.2. Computing Network Architecture

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                   GyberComputer Orchestrator             │
│    (smart contract + off-chain coordinator)              │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                          │
│   ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐   │
│   │   Node A     │  │   Node B     │  │   Node C     │   │
│   │ GPU: 2×A100  │  │ CPU: 32-core │  │ Storage: 10TB│   │
│   │ Role: AI     │  │ Role: DSP    │  │ Role: IPFS   │   │
│   │ Stake: 50K   │  │ Stake: 20K   │  │ Stake: 10K   │   │
│   └─────────────┘  └─────────────┘  └─────────────┘   │
│                                                          │
│   ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│   │              Resource Registry                   │   │
│   │  — Catalogue of available resources (CPU/GPU/RAM/SSD)│
│   │  — Matching: tasks ↔ nodes (by capabilities)   │   │
│   │  — Scheduling: task prioritisation              │   │
│   │  — Billing: accounting of consumed resources    │   │
│   └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Resource classes:**

| Class | Requirements | Stake | Application | Reward |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Compute-Light | 8+ CPU cores, 16GB RAM | 10,000 GBR | DSP hosting, IPFS pinning, indexing | 1× base_reward |
| Compute-Heavy | 32+ CPU cores, 64GB RAM | 25,000 GBR | cadCAD simulations, batch processing | 2× base_reward |
| GPU-Inference | 1+ GPU (RTX 3090+), 24GB VRAM | 50,000 GBR | AI model inference (LLM, GNN) | 3× base_reward |
| GPU-Training | 2+ GPU (A100+), 80GB+ VRAM | 100,000 GBR | Federated Learning, model training | 5× base_reward |
| Storage | 5TB+ SSD, 99.9% uptime | 10,000 GBR | IPFS pinning, archival storage | 1× base_reward × TB |

**Quality assurance mechanism:**

- **Proof of Computation:** for computational tasks — verifiable computation (optimistic verification: the result is accepted if none of k random validators challenged it within the challenge period)
- **Proof of Storage:** for storage nodes — periodic challenges: the orchestrator requests a Merkle proof for a random data block
- **Slashing:** upon failure to fulfil obligations (downtime, incorrect computations, data loss) — stake confiscation proportional to the severity of the violation

#### 4.5.3. Connection to the AiC Project

GyberComputer serves as the computational foundation for AiC (Artificial Intelligence Community, Section 4.8). Key integration points:

1. **Federated Learning:** AI models are trained distributedly on GyberComputer GPU nodes. Each node trains the model on local data and sends only gradient updates (not raw data) to an aggregating server. This ensures A3 (data sovereignty) while building high-quality AI models

2. **Model Registry:** trained models are stored in IPFS with on-chain metadata (version, quality metrics, authorship, AGPL licence). DAO manages access to models: internal models (free for participants), research models (open access), commercial models (licensable)

3. **Inference API:** API for AI model inference, distributed across GPU nodes with load balancing. Ecosystem participants invoke AI through a single endpoint; the orchestrator routes requests to the nearest available node

### 4.6. MacroeconomicDAO: Governance System

MacroeconomicDAO is the central mechanism for realising Axiom 7 (self-governance). It is a transparent system of interaction and decision-making, based on blockchain and verified Solidity smart contracts using the OpenZeppelin library.

#### 4.6.1. Governance Architecture

```
Technical implementation:

  Governor Contract (OpenZeppelin Governor):
— Deployed on BNB Smart Chain (BSC)
— Accepts proposals from GBR holders
— Manages voting: vote counting,
  quorum determination, result recording
— Transfers approved proposals to Timelock

  Timelock Contract:
    — Delay in the execution of approved decisions
      (24–48 hours — parameter determined by the community)
    — Provides the possibility of emergency response
      in the event of a malicious proposal being detected
    — Automatic execution after the delay expires

  Gnosis Safe (emergency multisig):
    — Emergency pause in the event of
      detection of a critical vulnerability
    — Keys held by trusted community members
      (determined by vote)
    — Cannot initiate expenditure — only pause
```

#### 4.6.2. Decision-Making Process

```
Standard governance cycle:

  1. Proposal:
     Any participant with an active wallet and sufficient
     GBR (Proposal Threshold) submits
     a proposal to the relevant DAO.

     Requirement: the wallet must be classified
     as "active" by the verification algorithm — this
     prevents governance capture by large but
     inactive holders.

  2. Discussion:
     The proposal is published in the project space
     of DSP associated with the relevant DAO.
     Discussion period: 1–2 days (Voting Delay).

  3. Voting:
     Upon expiry of the discussion period, voting opens.
     Voting period: 3–7 days.
     Quorum: 10–20% of total supply
     (specific parameters determined by the community).

     The voting mechanism may vary
     by DAO class and proposal type:
     simple majority, qualified
     majority, quadratic voting.

  4. Execution:
     Approved proposals are automatically queued
     in Timelock. Upon expiry of the delay —
     automatic execution of on-chain operations.

     For off-chain operations — authorised
     implementors begin work.

  5. Accountability:
     Execution results are recorded on-chain.
     Implementors report via DSP.
     The reputation system records the quality
     of execution.
```

#### 4.6.3. Four DAO Classes

MacroeconomicDAO unites four classes of decentralised organisations, each responsible for a specific category of decisions:

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    MacroeconomicDAO                           │
│              (meta-level of coordination)                     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────┐          ┌─────────────────┐            │
│  │   Social DAO     │          │    Code DAO      │           │
│  │                  │          │                  │           │
│  │ Community social │          │ Technical        │           │
│  │ life:            │          │ infrastructure:  │           │
│  │ norms, events,   │          │ codebase,        │           │
│  │ membership,      │          │ architecture,    │           │
│  │ disputes          │          │ standards        │           │
│  └─────────────────┘          └─────────────────┘            │
│                                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────┐          ┌─────────────────┐            │
│  │  Commerce DAO    │          │  Economic DAO    │           │
│  │                  │          │                  │           │
│  │ Commercial       │          │ Systemic         │           │
│  │ projects:        │          │ economic         │           │
│  │ crowd-investing, │          │ decisions:       │           │
│  │ business plans,  │          │ treasury,        │           │
│  │ profitability    │          │ strategy,        │           │
│  │                  │          │ large-scale      │           │
│  │                  │          │ projects         │           │
│  └─────────────────┘          └─────────────────┘            │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

> 📊 **Professional version:** [Open SVG](diagrams/process/dao_governance_flow.svg)

*Figure 4.3: Structure of MacroeconomicDAO, uniting four classes of decentralised autonomous organisations: Social DAO (community social life), Code DAO (technical infrastructure and codebase), Commerce DAO (commercial projects and crowd-investing), Economic DAO (systemic economic decisions and treasury management). MacroeconomicDAO functions as the meta-level of coordination among the classes.*

A detailed specification of each class is presented in Section 5.
#### 4.6.4. Voting Parameters by DAO Class

Each DAO class has its own set of voting parameters, optimised for the type of decisions being made. Parameters are determined by a vote of Economic DAO and are adapted as the ecosystem matures.

```
Voting Parameters:

  Social DAO (social decisions):
    Voting Delay:       1 day
    Voting Period:      3 days
    Quorum:             10% of total supply
    Proposal Threshold: 0.5% of total supply
    Timelock Delay:     24 hours
    Mechanism:          simple majority (>50%)
    Examples:           codes of conduct, event
                        organisation, dispute resolution,
                        appointment/replacement of Administrator

  Code DAO (technical decisions):
    Voting Delay:       2 days
    Voting Period:      5 days
    Quorum:             15% of total supply
    Proposal Threshold: 1% of total supply
    Timelock Delay:     48 hours
    Mechanism:          qualified majority
                        (>66%) for critical changes
    Examples:           merge into main branch, smart
                        contract upgrades, architectural
                        decisions, development standards
    Additional:         AI Code Reviewer must approve
                        the proposal before voting

  Commerce DAO (commercial decisions):
    Voting Delay:       2 days
    Voting Period:      7 days
    Quorum:             15% of total supply
    Proposal Threshold: 1% of total supply
    Timelock Delay:     48 hours
    Mechanism:          simple majority + mandatory
                        due diligence (AI analyst
                        generates report)
    Examples:           launch of a new project,
                        approval of a business plan,
                        determination of LP parameters

  Economic DAO (economic decisions):
    Voting Delay:       3 days
    Voting Period:      7 days
    Quorum:             20% of total supply
    Proposal Threshold: 2% of total supply
    Timelock Delay:     72 hours (or 7 days for
                        critical changes)
    Mechanism:          qualified majority
                        (>66%)
    Examples:           changes to staking parameters,
                        major treasury expenditures
                        (>$50,000), amendment of Governor
                        contract, blockchain migration

Proposal types by priority:
  Routine    (<$10K):  standard class parameters
  Significant ($10K–$50K): elevated quorum (+5%)
  Critical   (>$50K):  maximum quorum + 7-day
                        Timelock + mandatory AI audit
  Emergency  (security): Gnosis Safe → pause → then
                        standard governance for resolution
```

#### 4.6.5. Hybrid Voting Power: A Combined Voting Model

Standard token-weighted voting produces plutocracy: one token = one vote means that large holders dominate. GyberExperiment implements the Hybrid Voting Power model, combining three components:

```
Hybrid Voting Power Formula:

  VP(aᵢ) = √(GBR_staked(aᵢ)) × AM(aᵢ) × SB(statusᵢ)

  where:
    GBR_staked(aᵢ)  — number of GBR staked
                      by participant aᵢ in the Governor contract
    √()             — square root ensures
                      sub-quadratic scaling:
                      doubling the stake yields only √2 ≈ 1.41×
                      increase in voting power
    AM(aᵢ)          — Activity Multiplier, determined
                      by Activity Score (0–100):
                        score ∈ [0, 30)  → AM = 0.5
                        score ∈ [30, 60) → AM = 0.75
                        score ∈ [60, 80) → AM = 1.0
                        score ∈ [80, 100] → AM = 1.5
    SB(statusᵢ)     — Status Bonus:
                        Unit:    1.0
                        Dev:     1.1
                        LeadDev: 1.2
                        ArchDev: 1.3
                        Core:    1.5

Example:
  Participant A: 1,000,000 GBR staked, score=90, Dev
    VP(A) = √(1,000,000) × 1.5 × 1.1 = 1000 × 1.65 = 1,650

  Participant B: 10,000,000 GBR staked, score=20, Unit
    VP(B) = √(10,000,000) × 0.5 × 1.0 = 3162 × 0.5 = 1,581

  Result: participant A, with a 10× smaller stake, possesses
  MORE voting power than B, owing to high
  activity and Dev status. This realises Axiom A5
  (meritocratic fairness).

Model properties:
  — Completely eliminates linear plutocracy
  — Rewards active participants
  — Preserves economic incentives (staking)
  — Resistant to Sybil attacks: Activity Score
    requires genuine verified activity
  — Implemented via GBRVotingWrapper —
    a wrapper around OpenZeppelin Governor
```

#### 4.6.6. Cross-DAO Coordination

Decisions affecting multiple DAO classes simultaneously — for instance, the launch of a major project requiring commercial approval from Commerce DAO, technical approval from Code DAO, and economic approval from Economic DAO — pass through the Cross-DAO coordination mechanism.

```
Cross-DAO Mechanism:

  1. The initiator submits a multi-DAO proposal
     specifying the affected classes
  2. AI Cross-DAO Coordinator automatically
     routes the proposal to the relevant
     DAO contracts
  3. Each DAO votes independently according to its
     own parameters
  4. The proposal is considered approved only upon
     approval by ALL affected DAOs
  5. If any one DAO rejects → the entire proposal
     is returned for revision
  6. In the event of divergence → FRP (Conflict
     Fork Protocol, section 3.6.3)

Examples of Cross-DAO decisions:
  — Launch of a new project (Commerce + Code + Economic)
  — Upgrade of UnitManager (Code + Economic)
  — Amendment of membership rules (Social + Economic)
  — Integration of a new AI model (Code + Social)
```

#### 4.6.7. Wallet Activity Verification

A distinguishing feature of MacroeconomicDAO is the requirement for **wallet activity verification**. To participate in governance (voting and signing proposals), a tokenholder's wallet must be classified as "active" by a dedicated verification algorithm.

```
The verification algorithm checks:
  — Participation in ecosystem tasks (G-Plan data)
  — Engagement with projects (commits, discussions,
    funding)
  — Regularity of activity (not one-off actions,
    but a stable pattern of participation)

Objectives of the mechanism:
  — Preventing governance capture by inactive
    large holders
  — Ensuring that governance power is exercised
    by participants engaged in the current
    activities of the experiment
  — Aligning governance influence with active
    contribution rather than passive wealth
```

### 4.7. Legal Wrapper: Gybernaty DUNA

#### 4.7.1. Rationale for a Legal Form

The cyber-social corporation operates in the domain of blockchain and smart contracts; however, its interaction with the traditional economy — banking operations, contracts with counterparties, tax obligations, intellectual property protection — requires a legal entity. The choice of legal form is a critical decision: the wrong form could undermine Axioms A1 (decentralisation) and A7 (self-governance).

**The fundamental distinction: Gybernaty DUNA ≠ MacroeconomicDAO.** Gybernaty DUNA is a centralised legal gateway for the bootstrap phase of the experiment. It serves as an administrative shell enabling the organisers to conduct the experiment within the legal framework of the traditional economy: to open bank accounts, conclude contracts, and pay taxes. DUNA is deliberately centralised at this stage — the organisers retain control to ensure operational efficiency and the project's survivability in its early phase. MacroeconomicDAO, described in section 5, is the target state of full decentralisation towards which the experiment evolves as the community grows and the protocol matures. The transition from DUNA to MacroeconomicDAO is a planned trajectory, not a one-time event.

```
Selected form: DUNA (Decentralized Unincorporated
Nonprofit Association) — State of Wyoming, USA

Rationale:

  1. Specialised legal form for DAOs:
     DUNA was established in 2024 specifically for
     the recognition of on-chain governance within
     the legal framework. This means that decisions
     of the Governor contract carry legal force —
     a direct link between the smart contract and
     the legal entity.

  2. Elimination of fiduciary duties:
     DUNA permits the exclusion of fiduciary duties
     of members, enabling full reliance on code
     and voting. This is critically important for
     realising Axiom A7 (self-governance):
     decisions are made by algorithm, not by
     trusted individuals.

  3. Limitation of liability:
     Limits the liability of participants (community
     members) for the DAO's obligations —
     risk mitigation for participants.

  4. Nonprofit status:
     Revenue is reinvested rather than distributed
     as dividends. This is consistent with the CSC
     model, where the criterion of success is social
     relevance, not profit maximisation
     (Definition 3.2.1, point 6).

  5. Public identifier of the smart contract:
     The address of the Governor contract is
     specified upon registration — this creates a
     direct legal link between the legal entity and
     the on-chain governance mechanism.
```

#### 4.7.2. Control Architecture: Community → DUNA → Real World

        ```
        Principle of Absolute Control:

          Gybernaty Community (GBR holders)
            │
            │ on-chain voting
            │ via Governor + Timelock
            ▼
          Gybernaty DUNA (legal entity)
            │
            │ legally binding
            │ voting decisions
            ▼
          Administrator (Ministerial Agent)
            │
            │ technical execution:
            │ fiat payments, taxes, compliance
            ▼
          Traditional Economy
            (banks, counterparties, regulators)

        Key restrictions on Administrator:
          — Has no right to initiate expenditures
    without on-chain voting
  — Has no access to the crypto-treasury
    (no keys held)
  — Cannot block approved decisions
  — May be instantly replaced via
    a vote in Social DAO
  — Their role is exclusively technical
    execution: ministerial agent,
    not a manager

Two-tier treasury:

  Crypto-treasury (DAO governance):
    All crypto assets → Timelock contract
    Any movement → Governor vote
    Direct community control

  Fiat treasury:
    Treasury Fiat Account → governance via DAO
      (large payments, capital assets)
    Operating Fiat Account → Administrator
      (small operational expenditures within
       the approved budget, max $2,000
       per transaction)

    Replenishment of Operating Account → only
    via governance vote (e.g., $10K/month)

    Surpluses → automatic return
    to Treasury Account
```

#### 4.7.3. Mechanisms for Legal Value Extraction by Participants

Participants of CSC make real contributions — intellectual labour, code, research, coordination — and must receive remuneration for these. DUNA provides legal mechanisms for this purpose:

```
1. Compensation for services:
   Participants conclude a service contract
   with DUNA (strategic guidance, technical
    development, research, coordination).
   The amount of remuneration is approved by vote.
   Legal qualification: "reasonable compensation",
   permitted by law.

2. Research grants:
   DUNA issues grants for the development of new
   products, the conduct of research, and
   educational programmes.
   Grants are approved via Economic DAO or Social DAO.

3. Buyback & Burn:
   DUNA directs a portion of revenues towards
   the repurchase of GBR from a DEX and its burning.
   Legal qualification: "asset management operation
   to maintain protocol liquidity", and NOT a
   distribution of profits.
   Effect: deflationary pressure on supply → given
   stable demand → growth in GBR value → growth in
   the real value of remuneration through UnitManager.

All operations pass through a vote (the crypto portion
is executed automatically via Timelock; the fiat
portion — via Administrator).
```

#### 4.7.4. Compliance with Axioms

```
A1 (decentralisation):
  — DUNA has no single controlling party
  — Governance pool (~80%+) is distributed across
    dozens of wallets
  — No single participant holds <25% control

A2 (transparency):
  — All votes are on-chain on BSC
  — All crypto-treasury operations via Timelock
  — Monthly Administrator reports
  — Public dashboard (Dune Analytics)
  — Mandatory smart contract audit

A3 (sovereignty):
  — Every participant controls their own keys
  — No one has access to the wallets of others

A5 (meritocracy):
  — Remuneration is determined by activity (G-Plan)
    and status, not by token holdings

A6 (inclusivity):
  — Minimum barrier to entry
  — Limitation of liability via DUNA
  — Liquidity pools ensure participation in the
    success of any project

A7 (self-governance):
  — Governor contract = legally recognised
    governance mechanism
  — Administrator is subordinate to a vote
  — All critical decisions — via DAO

A8 (cognitive augmentation):
  — AI Administrator monitor: an autonomous agent
continuously analysing Administrator actions
for compliance with DAO decisions:
∀ action(Adm) : Verify(action, DAO_decisions) ∈ {compliant, alert}
  — Upon detection of a divergence (alert) —
automatic notification to Social DAO
with a detailed description of the violation
  — The AI monitor has no executive authority:
observation and notification only (watchdog principle)
  — Monitoring logs are recorded on-chain,
ensuring auditability of control
```

#### 4.7.5. Legal Constraints and Priorities

**Nonprofit constraint upon dissolution:** in accordance with Wyoming legislation, upon dissolution of DUNA, the association's assets may not be distributed among participants for their private benefit. Assets must be transferred to another nonprofit organisation with a similar mission. GBR token holders have no right to receive assets in exchange for tokens upon dissolution. This is a fundamental property of the nonprofit form, ensuring that the value of the ecosystem cannot be "privatised."

**Priority of the agreement over code:** in the event of a discrepancy between the text of the Association Agreement and the behaviour of the smart contracts, the Agreement takes legal precedence. Smart contracts are instruments for implementing the Agreement, not a substitute for it. Upon discovering a discrepancy, the community is obliged to bring the code into conformity with the Agreement through a vote. This is a legal reality that does not undermine the principle of algorithmic governance: code implements the law, it does not create it.

#### 4.7.6. Compliance, Tax, and Regulatory Obligations

The operation of DUNA as the legal shell of CSC gives rise to a set of regulatory obligations, the disregard of which creates legal risks for participants.

**Beneficial owners (FinCEN BOI Report).** Any participant with >25% control over DUNA is required to submit a Beneficial Ownership Information Report (FinCEN). The distribution of the Governance Pool across dozens of wallets ensures that no single participant exceeds the 25% threshold. However, FinCEN also requires disclosure of persons with "substantial control" (senior officers, important decision-makers). Penalties for non-disclosure are criminal.

**Tax obligations:**

```
DUNA as a legal entity:
  — Files Form 8832 to elect tax status
  — Then files Form 990-N (for nonprofits with
    income <$50,000) or Form 990/990-EZ
  — DUNA's income (LP trading fees, buyback)
    is subject to corporate income tax
  — Expenditures (salaries, grants, operational)
    reduce the taxable base

Participants (personal taxes):
  — Salaries and grants from DUNA are subject to
    income tax based on the participant's residence
  — Contractor participants receive Form 1099-NEC
    (for US residents) or W-8BEN (for
    non-residents)
  — KYC is mandatory for all payment recipients
    >$600 (IRS requirement)

Administrator:
  — Responsible for timely filing of returns
  — All expenditures on tax consultants
    are approved by vote
```

**AML/KYC obligations:**
- KYC of grant recipients: Administrator conducts KYC of all payment recipients >$600
- Wallet screening: Chainalysis or Elliptic for checking incoming/outgoing transactions (required for banking services)
- Travel Rule: for transfers >$3,000 — disclosure of recipient information (FATF)

**Insurance:**
- D&O Insurance: liability insurance for Administrator
- Smart Contract Insurance: Nexus Mutual for coverage of vulnerability risks
- General Liability: general DUNA insurance to protect against third-party claims

**Audit and reporting:**
- Smart contracts: mandatory audit of Governor, Timelock, UnitManager, LPBurnInitiator prior to production deployment (CertiK, OpenZeppelin, or Trail of Bits)
- Financial reporting: quarterly publication via DSP + annual report
- Public dashboard: on-chain treasury data via Dune Analytics
- Annual report: Form 990 (IRS) + public report for the community

#### 4.7.7. Risk Matrix and Mitigation

| Risk | Probability | Impact | Mitigation |
|---|---|---|---|
| Administrator refuses to execute a decision | Low | High | Immediate dismissal via Social DAO, contractual liability, financial sanctions, AI monitoring |
| Loss of access to wallets | Low | Critical | Distribution across dozens of wallets, backup seed phrases, Gnosis Safe multisig, documented recovery procedure |
| SEC classifies GBR as a security | Medium | Critical | Legal opinion (Howey Test), absence of dividends, buyback as asset management, wallet distribution, utility functions |
| Bank refuses service | Medium | Medium | Mercury, Relay, Wyoming Community Bank; preparation of compliance package; minimisation of fiat operations (Phase 1) |
| Smart contract errors | Medium | Critical | Audit (CertiK/OZ/ToB), standard OpenZeppelin contracts, bug bounty, Timelock delay, Gnosis Safe pause |
| Change in Wyoming legislation | Low | High | Monitoring, migration plan to LLC or alternative form |
| Conflict of interest (self-dealing) | Medium | Medium | Public disclosure, limitation to "reasonable compensation", AI audit, transparent reporting |
| IRS challenges nonprofit status | Low | High | Strict compliance with nonprofit rules, legal structuring of buyback, tax attorney consultations |
| BSC ceases operation / 51% attack | Very Low | Critical | Migration plan to an EVM-compatible network, off-chain backup copies of governance data |

#### 4.7.8. DUNA Roadmap

```
Stage 1 — Legal structuring:
  — Engagement of a law firm (Wyoming DUNA specialisation)
  — Drafting of Association Agreement
  — Contract with Administrator (Ministerial Agent Agreement)
  — Template contracts with participants

Stage 2 — Registration:
  — Filing Articles of Organization with Secretary of State
  — Obtaining EIN from IRS
  — Filing BOI Report (FinCEN)
  — Appointment of registered agent

Stage 3 — Technical implementation:
  — Deployment of Governor contract (BSC)
  — Deployment of Timelock contract (BSC)
  — Configuration of Gnosis Safe (emergency multisig)
  — Contract audit
  — Deployment of LPBurnInitiator

Stage 4 — Launch:
  — Vote to approve Association Agreement
  — Vote to appoint Administrator
  — First grants and compensation (governance vote)
  — Opening of fiat bank account
  — Transfer of assets to Timelock
  — Creation of LP positions on PancakeSwap
  — Locking LP via Team.Finance

Stage 5 — Automation (6–12 months):
  — Opening of Bridge Business Account (Treasury Fiat)
  — Development of Automation Contract with Chainlink Functions
  — Automated crypto→USD conversion
  — Programmatic wire transfers pursuant to governance decisions

Stage 6 — Full automation (12+ months):
  — 90%+ of operations without human involvement:
    Governance vote → Timelock → Chainlink Oracle →
    Bridge API → wire transfer
  — Administrator only for: Operating Account,
    compliance, emergency cases
```

### 4.8. AiC — Gybernaty Artificial Intelligence Department

#### 4.8.1. Status and Role in the Ecosystem

AiC (*Artificial Intelligence Community*) is not a standalone project among others — it is an **internal department** of Gybernaty Community, responsible for one of the key domains of computer science. Artificial intelligence permeates every aspect of the community's activities: from the automation of governance and verification of participant activity to the creation of fundamentally new products entering the open market. The integration of AI into the course of the experiment and into everything Gybernaty does is one of the key aspects of community development.

This status fundamentally distinguishes AiC from external AI startups or isolated research laboratories. AiC is embedded in the architecture of CSC as its intellectual layer — in the same way that the nervous system is embedded in an organism, rather than being a separate organ. Every component of the GyberExperiment ecosystem — DSP, G-Plan, MacroeconomicDAO, GyberComputer, GyberNet — is simultaneously a consumer and a supplier of AI solutions.

```
Position of AiC in the CyberSocium architecture:

                    ┌─────────────────────────────────┐
                    │        AiC Department            │
                    │   (Artificial Intelligence       │
                    │    Community)                    │
                    │                                  │
                    │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────────┐ │
                    │  │ Research │  │  Applied AI   │ │
                    │  │   Lab    │  │  Engineering  │ │

                    │       │               │         │
                    └───────┼───────────────┼─────────┘
                            │               │
          ┌─────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────────┐
          │                 │               │                │
          ▼                 ▼               ▼                ▼
    ┌───────────┐    ┌───────────┐   ┌───────────┐    ┌───────────┐
    │   DSP     │    │  G-Plan   │   │  Macro-   │    │  Gyber-   │
    │           │    │           │   │  economic │    │  Computer │
    │ • Recom-  │    │ • Auto-   │   │  DAO      │    │           │

    │   ations  │    │   activ-  │   │ • Proposal│    │   training│
    │ • Moder-  │    │   ity     │   │   analysis│    │ • Infer-  │

    │   chats   │    │ • Task    │   │           │    │   uted    │

          │                 │               │                │
          └─────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────────┘
                            │               │
                            ▼               ▼
                    ┌─────────────────────────────────┐
                    │      Open Market                 │
                    │  AI products and services based  │
                    │  on AiC models                   │
                    └─────────────────────────────────┘
```

> 📊 **Professional version:** [Open SVG](diagrams/architecture/aic_integration.svg)

*Figure 4.4: Position of AiC Department in the CyberSocium architecture. AiC functions as a horizontal AI infrastructure layer permeating all components of the ecosystem: DSP (recommendations, moderation, NLP, search, translation), G-Plan (automatic activity verification, task evaluation, distribution), MacroeconomicDAO (proposal analysis, forecasting), GyberComputer (model training, inference, distributed computing). AI products reach the open market via Commerce DAO.*

#### 4.8.2. The Problem AiC Addresses

The current state of the artificial intelligence industry is characterised by a paradox structurally identical to the Phase 4 paradox (platform capitalism) described in Section 3.3. A technology that is by its very nature the product of decades of open academic research — from Rosenblatt's perceptron (1958) to the Transformer by Vaswani et al. (2017) [51] — is being monopolised by a narrow circle of corporations that transform public knowledge into a proprietary product.

```
Structure of the problem:

  1. Concentration of resources:
     Training frontier models (GPT-4, Gemini, Claude)
     requires $50M–$500M+ in computational resources.
     This creates an oligopoly: only 5–7 organisations
     worldwide are capable of training models at this scale.

  2. Closedness:
     Despite the fact that fundamental architectures
     (Transformer, LSTM, CNN) are published in open
     papers and implemented in open libraries
     (TensorFlow, PyTorch), the final models —
     trained weights, training data, fine-tuning
     methods — are proprietary.

     The underlying paradox: open science → closed product.

  3. Control over data:
     AI models are trained on data generated by
     billions of users (text, images, interactions).
     Users receive neither control nor compensation
     for the contribution of their data to the
     creation of models worth billions of dollars.

     This is a direct reproduction of the problem
     described in Section 1.3: the appropriation of
     user data by obsolete economic institutions.

  4. Opacity:
     Closed models are black boxes.
     It is impossible to verify their safety,
     absence of bias, or conformity with stated
     properties. This is a direct violation of the
     transparency principle (Axiom A2).

  5. Economic inaccessibility:
     APIs of frontier models cost $0.01–$0.06 per 1K tokens.
     For large-scale usage (millions of requests)
     this amounts to hundreds of thousands of dollars
     per year — unaffordable for the majority of
     developers, researchers, and organisations in
     developing countries.

  6. Risk of dependency:
     Dependence on closed AI providers creates a
     strategic risk: the provider may change terms,
     revoke access, or impose censorship.
     This violates Axiom A3 (sovereignty) and Axiom A7
     (self-governance).
```
