The open AI movement (Meta's LLaMA, Mistral, Stability AI, EleutherAI) partially addresses problems 2 and 4, but does not resolve problems 1, 3, 5, and 6 — the models remain products of individual corporations or collectives not embedded within a sustainable economic system that provides long-term financing and democratic governance.

AiC proposes a systemic solution grounded in the theory of CyberSocium: **the development and use of AI models as a public good, financed through PMIP, governed through DAO, and deployed on the decentralised GyberComputer infrastructure**.

#### 4.8.3. AiC Architecture

```
Three functional circuits:

Circuit 1 — Internal (AI for the ecosystem):

  Integration of AI into all components of GyberExperiment.
  Goal: increase efficiency, automate processes,
  improve user experience.

  Applications:

  DSP:
    — Recommendation systems: personalisation
      of the news feed, project suggestions,
      matching of like-minded participants
    — Content moderation: automatic detection
      of spam, violations, and bad-faith behaviour
      without centralised censorship
      (federated moderation models)
    — NLP functions: automatic translation
      (critically important for global NFC),
      summarisation of discussions, extraction
      of key decisions from debates
    — Semantic search across projects,
      documentation, and codebase
    — AI assistants for new participants:
      onboarding, navigation of the ecosystem

  G-Plan:
    — Automatic activity verification:
      analysis of commits in repositories,
      participation in discussions, quality of
      completed tasks — to confirm activity
      when requesting rewards from UnitManager
    — Task complexity evaluation: automatic
      preliminary estimation of effort
      based on historical data
    — Optimal task distribution:
      matching of participants and tasks based on
      competencies, availability, and workload
    — Deadline forecasting: ML models
      for estimating implementation time
      based on project characteristics
      and historical data
    — Risk identification: early detection
      of problematic projects (slowdown in activity,
      decline in SIC engagement, conflicts in AG)

  MacroeconomicDAO:
    — Proposal analysis: automatic
      checking of completeness, consistency,
      and realism of proposals
    — Social relevance forecasting:
      ML models predicting |SIC(p)|
      based on project characteristics
    — Simulation of economic effects:
      modelling of the impact of proposed
      decisions on tokenomics, liquidity,
      and ecosystem growth
    — Anomaly detection: identification
      of suspicious voting patterns
      (Sybil attacks, coordinated
      manipulation)
    — Information aggregation for voters:
      automatic summaries of discussions,
      visualisation of arguments for/against

  GyberNet:
    — Network monitoring: anomaly detection
      in blockchain transactions
    — Optimisation of consensus parameters
    — Predictive load analytics

  GyberComputer:
    — Optimal distribution of computational
      tasks across nodes
    — Predictive resource scaling
    — Monitoring of node performance

Circuit 2 — Research (AI science):

  Organisation and conduct of fundamental
  and applied research in the field of AI.
  Goal: advancing science and building
  the intellectual capacity of the community.

  Directions:
    — Distributed model training
      (federated learning, distributed training)
    — Private machine learning
      (differential privacy, homomorphic encryption
       for training on confidential data)
    — AI alignment and safety
      (open research, critically
       important for society)
    — Efficient architectures for edge devices
      (models running on participants'
       devices, without cloud infrastructure)
    — Multimodal models
      (text, images, audio, video, code)
    — AI for scientific discovery
      (drug discovery, materials science,
       climate modeling — via Economic DAO)

  Organisation:
    — Research groups are formed
      as SIC/AG within the IPI model
    — Financing via Economic DAO
      or DUNA grants
    — Results are published as open access
      (AGPL for code, CC-BY for papers)
    — Peer review within the community
      and in international journals

Circuit 3 — Commercial (AI products):

  Creation of AI products and services for
  the open market. Goal: generation of revenue
  for the ecosystem (Loop 2 — liquidity).

  Model:
    — AI products are developed via IPI
      (as any ecosystem project)
    — Products utilise models developed
      in Circuit 2 and the infrastructure of Circuit 1
    — Market entry: via Commerce DAO
    — Tokenomics: project internal tokens →
      liquidity pool with GBR → DEX
    — Client tiers:
      external (fiat), special (GBR),
      super-clients (project tokens)

  Examples of potential products:
    — AI as a Service (AIaaS) platform
      on GyberComputer
    — Specialised models for verticals:
      medicine, finance, education, law
    — Automation tools for developers
    — AI analytics for blockchain projects
    — Private AI assistants
      (running on the user's device,
       without sending data to servers)
```

#### 4.8.4. AiC Technical Stack

```
Programming languages:
  — Python: primary language for ML/AI
    (TensorFlow, PyTorch, Keras, Scikit-learn,
     OpenCV, Hugging Face Transformers,
     LangChain, JAX)
  — C++: high-performance components,
    inference engines (ONNX Runtime, TensorRT)
  — Rust: safe system components,
    WASM modules for edge inference,
    integration with blockchain infrastructure
  — TypeScript: AI integrations in DSP,
    web interfaces for AI tools
  — Solidity: smart contracts for DAO governance
    of AI resources

Frameworks and libraries:
  — Training: PyTorch (primary), TensorFlow, JAX
  — Distributed training: DeepSpeed,
    Megatron-LM, Hivemind,
    PyTorch Distributed
  — Inference: vLLM, TGI, ONNX Runtime,
    llama.cpp, ExLlamaV2
  — Computer Vision: OpenCV, Detectron2,
    Segment Anything
  — NLP: Hugging Face ecosystem, spaCy, NLTK
  — MLOps: MLflow, Weights & Biases, DVC
  — Privacy: PySyft, OpenDP,
    Microsoft SEAL (homomorphic encryption)

Blockchain integration:
  — Ethereum/BSC: DAO contracts for governance
    of AI resources and models
  — TON: potential platform for
    AI micropayments (high throughput,
    low fees)
  — Solana: high-performance AI applications
    with on-chain components
  — IPFS/Filecoin: decentralised storage
    of training data and model weights

Licensing:
  — All AiC code: AGPL-3.0
    (guarantees that any modifications
     and derivative works remain open)
  — Trained models: open weights
    (licence determined for each model
     by vote in Code DAO)
  — Research publications: CC-BY-4.0
  — Training data: open datasets
    or data collected with the explicit consent
    of participants (Axiom A3 — data sovereignty)
```

#### 4.8.5. DAO Governance of AI Resources

One of the fundamental innovations of AiC is the governance of AI models and resources through DAO mechanisms. This provides democratic control over a technology that, in the traditional model, is controlled exclusively by corporate management.

```
Decisions made through DAO:

  Code DAO:
    — Adoption of architectural decisions
      (selection of base models, frameworks)
    — Merge of pull requests into primary
      AI code repositories
    — Approval of code quality and documentation
      standards
    — Decisions on model licensing

  Social DAO:
    — Prioritisation of research directions
    — Ethical issues: permissible and impermissible
      applications of AI models
    — Data policy:
      what data is used for training,
      how privacy is ensured
    — Organisation of AI conferences, hackathons,
      and educational programmes within the community

  Commerce DAO:
    — Approval of AI products for launch
      on the commercial market
    — Pricing of AI services
    — Partnerships with external organisations

  Economic DAO:
    — Financing of major research
      programmes (training of large models,
      GPU procurement, data collection)
    — Distribution of GyberComputer computational
      resources among AiC tasks
    — Investments in AI infrastructure
```

#### 4.8.6. AiC Economic Model

```
Funding sources:

  1. Gybernaty internal budget
     — Allocation from DUNA treasury via
       Economic DAO vote
     — Targeted financing of infrastructure
       (GPU clusters, data storage)

  2. Grants and partnerships
     — Decentralised grant programmes
       (Ethereum Foundation, Protocol Labs, etc.)
     — Academic partnerships
       with research institutions
     — Corporate partnerships for
       applied AI solutions

  3. Commercial revenues (Circuit 3)
     — AIaaS (AI as a Service) on
       GyberComputer
     — Licensing of specialised models
     — Consulting and AI solution integration
     — Private AI assistants for enterprises

  4. AiC tokenomics
     — Issuance of AiC internal token
       via the IPI model (Section 3.4)
     — AiC/GBR liquidity pool on DEX
     — Staking: 10 / [total number of
       AiC tokens] % of project revenue
```

**Revenue distribution:**

```
  ┌──────────────────────────────────────┐
  │        AiC PROJECT REVENUES          │
  ├──────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                                      │
  │  40% → AiC token holders             │
  │        (SIC participants)            │
  │                                      │
  │  25% → Operational expenditures      │
  │        (infrastructure, GPU,         │
  │         data storage)                │
  │                                      │
  │  20% → Reinvestment in research      │
  │        (Circuit 2 — AI science)      │
  │                                      │
  │  10% → Gybernaty treasury            │
  │        (via GBR LP)                  │
  │                                      │
  │   5% → Staking rewards               │
  │        (for AiC token stakers)       │
  │                                      │
  └──────────────────────────────────────┘
```

| Direction | Share | Purpose |
|------------|------|------------|
| **AiC token holders** | 40% | Remuneration of SIC participants |
| **Operational expenditures** | 25% | Infrastructure, GPU, data storage |
| **Reinvestment in research** | 20% | Circuit 2 — AI science |
| **Gybernaty treasury** | 10% | Via GBR/AiC liquidity pool |
| **Staking rewards** | 5% | For AiC token stakers |

*Table 4.1: Distribution of revenues from AiC projects. All revenues pass through the AiC/GBR liquidity pool, providing a direct link between AiC's success and the value of the GBR ecosystem — realisation of Loop 2 (liquidity).*

  Key mechanism: all revenues pass
  through the AiC/GBR liquidity pool, which
  provides a direct link between AiC's success
  and the value of the GBR ecosystem —
  realisation of Loop 2 (liquidity)
  from the project lifecycle model.
```

#### 4.8.7. The Cyber-Social Significance of AiC

AiC represents the application of cyber-social principles to the technology that is arguably the most significant for the current era. By demonstrating that frontier AI development can be organised through decentralised, community-governed structures, AiC challenges the assumption that only centralised corporations with massive capital reserves are capable of participating in the advancement of the AI frontier.

AiC also provides a model for the democratic governance of AI systems — a critically important need in an era when artificial intelligence is increasingly shaping economic, social, and political outcomes. Within AiC:

- **Decisions on research priorities** are made through community voting, not by a corporate board of directors
- **Training data** is collected with explicit consent and under the control of participants (Axiom A3)
- **Trained models** are available to all participants and licensed as open (AGPL for code, open weights for models)
- **Revenues from commercialisation** are distributed among participants through transparent smart contracts, rather than being appropriated by shareholders

#### 4.8.8. Applied AI Engineering: Concrete Implementations

Based on an analysis of the current state of the AI industry (2026) and the GyberExperiment architecture, the following describes concrete AI integration points — from the most mature (production-ready) to experimental.

**1. AI Governance Agents (maturity level: high).**

The problem of voter fatigue in DAOs is addressed by three types of AI agents:

- *AI proposal summariser* — an agent that analyses each proposal and generates a structured summary: essence, risks, economic consequences, arguments for/against. Integrated with Governor contracts via API.
- *AI delegate with limited mandate* — an agent that votes on routine matters in Social DAO and Code DAO according to pre-established rules (constraint-first governance), with a mandatory human override right. Identified by a soulbound token.
- *Consequences simulator* — before a vote, models: "if this proposal passes, here is what will happen to the treasury / liquidity / GyberComputer load". Uses cadCAD models (section 6.3).

Technology stack: CrewAI (multi-agent orchestration), open-source LLM (Llama, Mixtral) on GyberComputer for sovereignty, ETHOS-like system (soulbound tokens for agent identification, ZK-proofs for decision auditing).

**2. Continuous AI Audit Pipeline (maturity level: production-ready).**

Every pull request with Solidity code changes automatically passes through a multi-level AI audit:

```
CI/CD AI Audit Architecture:

  Git Push → GitHub Actions
    │
    ├─ Level 1: Static analysis
    │  (Slither, Mythril — deterministic)
    │
    ├─ Level 2: AI audit
    │  (Octane Security, Sherlock AI, AuditAgent)
    │  — analysis of logical vulnerabilities
    │  — simulation of attack scenarios
    │  — comparison with the database of past exploits
    │
    ├─ Level 3: Formal verification
    │  (critical invariants of UnitManager,
    │   Governor, Timelock)
    │
    └─ Result:
       Critical vulnerability → block merge
         + alert to Core/ArchDev
       Warning → comment in PR
         + review in Code DAO
       Clean → admission to Code DAO vote

  Deployed contracts:
    Chainalysis AI monitoring → alerts
    to Gnosis Safe signers upon anomalies
```

Specific tools: Octane Security (CI/CD-native, helped protect >$8M in a real DeFi protocol), Sherlock AI (analysis during code writing), AuditAgent (Nethermind, trained on real audits), ChainGPT Auditor (trained on historical exploits), OpenZeppelin AI tools (reduce audit time by 50%).

**3. AI-powered Reputation Engine (maturity level: medium-high).**

To ensure Sybil resistance and reliable Activity Scoring:

- *Graph Neural Network for Sybil detection* — PyTorch Geometric on GyberComputer: analysis of the wallet interaction graph, detection of clusters of fake/coordinated accounts.
- *Proof of Personhood* — ZK cryptography (Circom/Halo2) for one-person-one-identity without disclosure of personal data.
- *Anomaly Detection* — ML models for detecting unusual activity patterns: farming (performing minimal tasks for Activity Score), wash trading of tasks in G-Plan, coordinated voting.
- *Reputation-weighted ranking* — every action = endorsement, the strength of which depends on reputation; AI forms a dynamic ranking via Soulbound tokens (SBT).

**4. Federated Learning on GyberComputer (maturity level: medium-high).**

Axiom A3 (data sovereignty) prohibits centralised data collection for model training. Federated Learning resolves this conflict:

```
Federated Learning Architecture:

  GyberComputer nodes:
    │
    ├─ Node 1: local data → local
    │          training → prototype/gradients
    ├─ Node 2: local data → local
    │          training → prototype/gradients
    ├─ Node N: ...
    │
    └─► Aggregator (on GyberComputer):
          — Federated Averaging / PearFL aggregation
          — Differential Privacy (PySyft, OpenDP)
          — Updated global model → back
            to nodes
          — Recording of training round on-chain (GyberNet)
          — GBR reward to participants for
            providing data/computation

  Framework: Flower (de facto FL standard, 2026)
  Protocol: PearFL (Prototype Exchange —
    exchange of lightweight prototypes instead of gradients,
    minimising communication overhead)
  Privacy: Differential Privacy + PySyft
  Incentives: GBR rewards via UnitManager
```

Federated Learning enables AiC models to be trained without violating the data sovereignty of participants: data never leaves the user's device; the model comes to the data, not the other way around. This fundamentally distinguishes AiC from centralised AI companies, which require the transfer of data to their servers.

**5. cadCAD Ecosystem Simulation (maturity level: high).**

To model the economic effects of proposed decisions and optimise tokenomics parameters, cadCAD (complex adaptive dynamics Computer Aided Design) is used — an agent-based modelling framework developed by BlockScience (M. Zargham):

- Modelling of token velocity, emission/burning, LP liquidity
- Stress testing: what will happen with 10× participant growth? With a market crash? With a coordinated Sybil attack?
- Parameter optimisation: quorum, voting period, staking rewards, LP Burn threshold
- A/B testing of governance parameters before a real vote

Each Economic DAO proposal is accompanied by a cadCAD simulation demonstrating the expected consequences across 10,000+ scenarios. This transforms governance from a political process into a data-driven engineering discipline
- **Ethical constraints** are established democratically through Social DAO, ensuring public control over AI applications

In this way, AiC is not merely a technical project, but an **institutional innovation** — a new model for organising the development and governance of technologies that define humanity's future.

#### 4.8.9. AiC as the Infrastructure AI Layer of the Ecosystem

The three AiC circuits described above (Internal, Research, Commercial) possess yet another, fundamental dimension: AiC is an **infrastructure layer** providing AI augmentation of all processes of the cyber-social corporation. It is not a standalone project alongside DSP, GyberNet, and G-Plan — it is a horizontal layer permeating all elements of the ecosystem.

```
Architectural position of AiC in the ecosystem:

  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │        Application layer                          │
  │   DSP    G-Plan    GyberNet    Commerce projects  │
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │        AiC — AI infrastructure layer              │
  │                                                    │
  │  ┌────────────┬────────────┬─────────────────┐    │
  │  │ AI analyst │ AI coordi- │ AI assistant    │    │
  │  │ (E1, SES)  │ nator(PMIP)│ (IPI, FRP)     │    │
  │  ├────────────┼────────────┼─────────────────┤    │
  │  │ AI auditor │ AI monitor │ AI knowledge    │    │
  │  │ (Code DAO) │ (Economic) │ base(E6, cumul.)│    │
  │  └────────────┴────────────┴─────────────────┘    │
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │        Blockchain layer (BSC, GyberNet)            │
  │   Governor    UnitManager    Tokens    LP pools    │
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

> 📊 **Professional version:** [Open SVG](diagrams/architecture/aic_infrastructure_layer.svg)

*Figure 4.5: Architectural position of AiC in the ecosystem as a horizontal layer permeating all levels. Top level — applications (DSP, G-Plan, GyberNet, Commerce projects), middle level — AiC with six types of AI agents (AI analyst for SES and E1, AI coordinator for PMIP, AI assistant for IPI and FRP, AI auditor for Code DAO, AI monitor for Economic DAO, AI knowledge base for experience accumulation E6), bottom level — blockchain (Governor, UnitManager, tokens, LP pools). Each component of the top level accesses AI services through a standardised API.*

**Relationship of AiC to theoretical constructs:**

| Theoretical element | AiC function | Result |
|---|---|---|
| Axiom A8 (Cognitive augmentation) | AiC — institutional realisation of A8 | Democratic control over AI augmentation |
| PMIP: C(p) → min | AI coordinator reduces project costs | individual_cost(p \| AI) < individual_cost(p) |
| SES: project selection | AI predictor of SR improves selection quality | Directed evolution instead of blind selection |
| E1: collective intelligence | AI analyst compensates for cognitive limitations | Scaling without loss of quality |
| E2: antifragility | AI monitor ensures preventive adaptation | Active antifragility |
| E6: knowledge accumulation | AI knowledge base indexes all experience | Exponential knowledge growth |
| FRP: fork resolution | AI mediator reduces the cost of Deliberation | FRP from costly process → routine |

**Principle of horizontality:** each element of the ecosystem accesses AiC AI services through a standardised API. DSP uses AI for discussion summarisation and recommendations. G-Plan uses AI for optimal task assignment and deadline forecasting. GyberNet uses AI for optimisation of consensus parameters. Commerce projects receive AI code review, security audit, and analytics. At the same time, all AI services are subject to the division principle (Axiom A8): AI decides, AI informs, AI has no authority — depending on the class of the task.

**Economic model of the AI layer:**

```
Financing of AiC infrastructure:

  1. Basic AI services → financed from the treasury
     (public good, available to all participants)

  2. Advanced AI services → freemium model
     (basic access is free, extended access — for GBR)

  3. Commercial AI products (Circuit 3) →
     revenue returns to the ecosystem via
     distribution smart contracts

  This creates a self-sustaining cycle:
  AI layer augments the ecosystem → ecosystem grows →
  more data and resources for AI → AI is augmented →
  ecosystem is augmented further

  Formally: positive feedback loop 7
  (AI Flywheel):
  quality(AI) ↑ → productivity(CSC) ↑ →
  revenue(ecosystem) ↑ → investment(AiC) ↑ →
  quality(AI) ↑
```

In this way, AiC closes the theoretical cycle: Axiom A8 defines the *principles* of AI augmentation, the theoretical sections (PMIP, SES, E1–E6) describe the *mechanisms*, and AiC provides the *institutional and infrastructural realisation*, subject to community governance through the four-class DAO system.

---
## 5. DAO Taxonomy: A Four-Class Model of Decentralised Decision-Making

A distinguishing feature of the GyberExperiment governance architecture is the **four-class DAO taxonomy** — a structured classification of decentralised governance mechanisms that accounts for the different categories of collective decision-making. This taxonomy reflects the recognition that not all decisions are alike in their nature, and that different types of decisions may require different governance processes, participation criteria, and enforcement mechanisms.

### 5.1 Social DAO

#### 5.1.1 Purpose

Social DAOs govern the **internal social life of the community** — decisions concerning community norms, social events, membership policies, communication standards, dispute resolution procedures, and other matters pertaining to the community as a social entity rather than as an economic or technical enterprise.

#### 5.1.2 Scope

Social DAO decisions include, but are not limited to:

- Organisation of community events (conferences, hackathons, meetups, educational programmes)
- Establishment and modification of community codes of conduct
- Decisions regarding community communication channels and platforms
- Membership and participation policies
- Recognition and rewards for contributions to community life
- Cultural and educational initiatives

#### 5.1.3 Characteristics

- **Low economic stakes:** Social DAO decisions are generally not associated with significant financial resources (although they may include the allocation of small event budgets).
- **Broad participation:** All community members may participate in Social DAO governance, reflecting the principle that social decisions should reflect the widest possible consensus.
- **Simple majority:** Most Social DAO decisions may be adopted by a simple majority vote, given their relatively low stakes and reversibility.
- **High frequency:** Social decisions arise frequently in the day-to-day life of the community, requiring lightweight governance processes that do not create excessive overhead.

#### 5.1.4 Formal Governance Parameters

```
Social DAO Parameters:

  Quorum: 5% of the total number of active participants
  (active = Activity Score ≥ 20)

  Discussion period: 48 hours
  Voting period: 72 hours
  Approval threshold: >50% (simple majority)

  Proposal rights:
    — Any participant with status ≥ Unit
    — Minimum staking: 100 GBR

  Voting rights:
    — All participants with status ≥ Unit
    — Weight: 1 vote per participant (one-person-one-vote)
    — Exception: membership proposals require
      Activity Score ≥ 30

  Execution:
    — Automatic via Timelock (24h delay)
    — Off-chain decisions: published on DSP,
      take effect after Timelock

  Budget constraints:
    — Maximum budget of a single proposal:
      500 GBR (for events)
    — Excess → escalation to Economic DAO
```

#### 5.1.5 Process Model: From Initiative to Execution

The proposal life cycle in Social DAO is formalised as the following finite-state machine:

```
[Initiative] → [Discussion, 48h] → [Voting, 72h]
    │                                        │
    │                                   ┌────┴────┐
    │                                   │         │
    │                               Approved  Rejected
    │                                   │         │
    │                              [Timelock]  [Archive]
    │                               (24h)
    │                                   │
    │                              [Execution]
    │                                   │
    │                            [Monitoring, 30 days]
    │                                   │
    └─ Retry: no earlier than ─── [Completion]
       14 days after rejection
```

**Typical Social DAO precedents:**

1. *Organisation of a hackathon.* The author proposes the format, date, and budget (≤500 GBR in prizes). Discussion: the community adjusts the parameters. Vote: simple majority. Execution: funds are allocated from the social pool, and the organiser reports via G-Plan.

2. *Update to the code of conduct.* The author proposes a new edition. Discussion period: extended to 7 days (by decision of moderators). Vote: simple majority. Execution: the new edition is published on DSP and all participants are notified.

3. *Exclusion of a participant for violation of the code of conduct.* A qualified majority (67%) is required, as fundamental rights are affected. Mandatory procedure: warning → repeated violation → exclusion proposal → vote. The excluded participant may appeal the decision through FRP.

### 5.2 Code DAO

#### 5.2.1 Purpose

Code DAOs govern the **technical infrastructure of the community** — in particular, the codebase of the DSP platform and other shared technical assets. The current state of the platform code is determined by the state of the main branch of the GitHub repository, and changes to that branch require passage through the Code DAO process.

#### 5.2.2 Scope

Code DAO decisions include:

- Merging proposed code changes (pull requests) into the main branch
- Approving new modules for inclusion in the standard node configuration
- Selection of technical standards and architectural patterns
- Evaluation and approval of security-critical changes
- Management of deprecation and removal of obsolete components
- Resolution of technical disputes between competing implementations

#### 5.2.3 Characteristics

- **Requirement of technical competence:** Voting in Code DAO may be weighted by technical reputation — participants with a confirmed track record of development contributions carry greater weight in technical decisions. This reflects the principle that technical decisions should be determined by technical expertise, while remaining transparent and contestable.
- **Review process:** Proposals in Code DAO typically include a mandatory technical review period, during which qualified community members examine the proposed changes for correctness, security, performance, and architectural consistency.
- **Meritocratic governance:** Although any community member may propose code changes, voting rights on technical matters are concentrated among those who have demonstrated relevant competence through their contribution history.
- **Awareness of irreversibility:** Code changes in production systems may have significant consequences. Code DAO processes include mechanisms for staged deployment, testing requirements, and rollback procedures.
- **Continuous AI security audit (from A8):** Every pull request affecting smart contracts (Solidity/Vyper) automatically passes through an AI audit pipeline before being admitted to a Code DAO vote. The pipeline includes:

```
AI Audit Pipeline (AiC implementation, Circuit 1):

  Git Push → CI/CD (GitHub Actions) → AI scanning:
    │
    │  Tools:
    │    — Octane Security: CI/CD-native analysis,
    │      detection of exploitable vulnerabilities
    │    — Sherlock AI: in-development analysis,
    │      targeted remediation
    │    — AuditAgent (Nethermind): attack scenario simulation
    │      based on real-world audits
    │
    ├─ Critical vulnerability →
    │    merge block + alert to ArchDev + Core
    ├─ Warning →
    │    comment in PR + mandatory review
    └─ Clear →
         admission to Code DAO vote

  Deployed contracts → continuous monitoring
  of anomalous transaction patterns → alerts
  to Gnosis Safe signers
```

  The AI audit does not replace human review but complements it: models detect patterns that a human may miss, while a human assesses context and business logic inaccessible to the model. Audit parameters (sensitivity thresholds, list of checked vulnerabilities) are determined by Code DAO vote.

#### 5.2.4 Formal Governance Parameters

```
Code DAO Parameters:

  Quorum: 10% of participants with status ≥ Dev
  (critical: technical decisions must be made
   by technically competent participants)

  Technical review period: 96 hours (minimum)
    — For smart contracts: 7 days + AI audit
    — For architectural decisions: 14 days
  Voting period: 96 hours
  Approval threshold:
    — Routine changes (bug fixes, dependency updates): >50%
    — Functional changes (new features): >60%
    — Architectural changes: >67% + cadCAD impact analysis
    — Smart contracts: >75% + AI audit clear + ≥2 independent reviews

  Proposal rights:
    — Any participant with status ≥ Unit
      (pull request is open to all)
    — Minimum staking: 500 GBR

  Voting rights:
    — Participants with status ≥ Dev
    — Weight determined by technical reputation:
      VP_code = code_contributions × review_quality × seniority
    — code_contributions: number of accepted PRs in the past year
    — review_quality: average review score from other developers
    — seniority: multiplier from MemberStatus (Dev=1×, LeadDev=1.5×,
      ArchDev=2×, Core=3×)

  Mandatory checks before admission to vote:
    — CI/CD pipeline passed (100% unit tests, ≥80% coverage)
    — Linting passed (ESLint + Prettier)
    — AI audit completed (for Solidity code)
    — ≥1 approve from a participant with status ≥ LeadDev
    — Does not violate existing API contracts (breaking changes
      require a migration plan)

  Rollback procedure:
    — Any change may be rolled back via
      emergency vote of ≥3 ArchDev/Core (without full quorum)
    — Emergency rollback: any 2 Core within 24h
    — After rollback: mandatory post-mortem analysis
```

#### 5.2.5 Process Model: From PR to Merge

The life cycle of a code change in Code DAO:

```
[Fork / Branch]
    │
    ▼
[Development + local tests]
    │
    ▼
[Pull Request] → [CI/CD Pipeline]
    │                    │
    │               ┌────┴────┐
    │            Passed    Failed
    │               │         │
    │               ▼      [Fix → retry]
    │         [AI audit]
    │            (Solidity only)
    │               │
    │          ┌────┴────┐
    │        Clear   Alert
    │          │       │
    │          │    [Fix/justification]
    │          │       │
    │          ▼       ▼
    │     [Peer Review: ≥1 LeadDev+]
    │               │
    │          ┌────┴────┐
    │       Approved  Changes Requested
    │          │            │
    │          │      [Fix → retry]
    │          ▼
    │    [Code DAO vote, 96h]
    │               │
    │          ┌────┴────┐
    │       Accepted  Rejected
    │          │         │
    │    [Timelock 24h] [Archive / FRP]
    │          │
    │    [Auto-merge → main]
    │          │
    │    [Deploy pipeline]
    │          │
    └─── [Monitoring 7 days]
```

**Typical Code DAO precedents:**

1. *Dependency update (routine).* A developer upgrades React 18→19. CI/CD passes, unit tests are green. One approve from a LeadDev. Vote: 48h, simple majority. Merge after 24h Timelock.

2. *New smart contract (critical).* A developer proposes LPBurnInitiator.sol. AI audit identifies 0 critical, 2 low issues (gas optimisation). Two independent reviews from ArchDev. Vote: 96h, threshold 75%. After approval: Timelock 48h. Deploy to testnet → 7 days monitoring → deploy to mainnet.

3. *Architectural decision (strategic).* Proposal to migrate from REST to GraphQL for GPROD API. The author provides: RFC document, proof-of-concept, performance benchmarks, migration plan. Discussion: 14 days. Vote: 96h, threshold 67%. If approved: a working group is formed in G-Plan for staged migration.

4. *Emergency security patch.* AI monitoring detects anomalous activity on UnitManager. Emergency pause activated (AI decision). Developer publishes a hotfix. Accelerated review: 2 ArchDev/Core within 24h. Vote: 24h (emergency mode), threshold 50%. Deploy → unpause. Post-mortem required within 7 days.

#### 5.2.6 Open Source Governance: Distinctive Features of Code DAO

Code DAO implements a unique open-source governance model that differs both from traditional corporate governance (proprietary, closed) and from classical open source (BDFL — Benevolent Dictator For Life, as in Linux or Python).

**Comparative table of code governance models:**

| Parameter | Corporate | BDFL (Linux) | Meritocracy (Apache) | Code DAO (CSC) |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Who decides | CTO / Tech Lead | One person (Torvalds) | Committers committee | DAO vote |
| Decision criterion | Business value | Technical quality | Technical quality + consensus | VP_code × vote |
| Transparency | Closed discussions | Public mailing lists | Public discussions | On-chain + DSP |
| Fork right | No (proprietary) | Yes (GPL) | Yes (Apache License) | Yes (FRP protocol) |
| AI audit | Internal (if any) | None | Partial | Mandatory |
| Accountability | To shareholders | To community (informally) | To Foundation | On-chain, verifiable |
| Incentives | Salary | Reputation, interest | Reputation | GBR + reputation + status |
| Key-person risk | High | Critical | Medium | Minimal |

Code DAO reduces key-person risk, which is a fundamental problem for open-source projects. In the BDFL model (Linux, Python, Ruby), the departure of a key person creates a succession crisis. In the Code DAO model, decisions are made in a distributed manner: no single developer, however talented, holds unilateral authority over the codebase. At the same time, technical competence in decisions is preserved: the VP_code formula ensures that voting weight correlates with actual contribution to development and technical authority.

### 5.3 Commerce DAO

#### 5.3.1 Purpose

Commerce DAOs implement the concept of **decentralised crowd-investment** — allowing entrepreneurs and enthusiasts within the community to propose business ideas or formal business plans for realisation using collective community resources, providing investors with the opportunity to receive a share of the resulting profit.

#### 5.3.2 Scope

Commerce DAO decisions include:

- Evaluation and approval of proposed commercial projects
- Determination of the terms for the issuance and sale of internal tokens
- Determination of profit-sharing schemes between executors and investors
- Approval of partnerships and client agreements
- Management of project budgets and financial reporting
- Decisions regarding the continuation, modification, or termination of a project based on results

#### 5.3.3 Characteristics

- **Economic stakes:** Commerce DAO decisions involve significant financial resources and economic risk. Governance processes are correspondingly more stringent.
- **Due diligence:** Proposals in Commerce DAO undergo a structured evaluation process comprising market analysis, technical feasibility assessment, financial projections, and risk evaluation.
- **Investor protection:** Smart contracts governing Commerce DAO projects include mechanisms for fund custody, milestone-based staged release, transparent accounting, and (in certain circumstances) fund return.
- **Results-based accountability:** Commercial projects are subject to regular performance reporting, with defined metrics and benchmarks. Sustained unsatisfactory performance may initiate governance actions, including management change or project restructuring.

#### 5.3.4 Relationship to the IPI Model

Commerce DAOs serve as the governance layer for phases 3–5 of the project life cycle (Accumulation, Implementation, Operation) for projects with commercial objectives. They operationalise the concept of the social-investment circle for revenue-generating projects.

#### 5.3.5 Formal Governance Parameters

```
Commerce DAO Parameters:

  Quorum: 15% of the total number of active participants
  with status ≥ Dev

  Discussion period: 7 days (includes due diligence)
  Voting period: 5 days
  Approval threshold:
    — Standard projects (C(p) < 10,000 GBR): >50%
    — Large projects (C(p) ≥ 10,000 GBR): >60%
    — Strategic projects (C(p) ≥ 100,000 GBR):
      >67% + Economic DAO approval

  Proposal rights:
    — Participants with status ≥ Dev
    — Minimum staking: 1,000 GBR
    — Required: business plan, financial projections,
      risk assessment

  Voting rights:
    — Participants with status ≥ Dev
    — Weight: Hybrid Voting Power
      VP = √(GBR_staked) × activity_multiplier
    — SIC(p) investors: additional weight
      proportional to investment

  Due diligence process:
    — AI agent analyses the business plan: market fit,
      competitive analysis, financial model
    — Technical review from Code DAO (for projects
      with a technical component)
    — DUNA legal analysis for compliance risks
    — Due diligence results are published
      as an annex to the proposal

  Investor protection mechanisms:
    — Escrow contract: funds are allocated
      by milestones
    — Milestone voting: SIC(p) votes for
      the release of each tranche
    — Emergency stop: Core + ArchDev may
      freeze a project upon critical violations
    — Refund mechanism: upon non-fulfilment of milestones,
      remaining funds are returned to investors
```

#### 5.3.6 Commercial Project Life Cycle

```
Full Commerce DAO project cycle:

  [Idea] ─── author publishes concept
      │
  [Discussion, 7 days] ─── community feedback
      │
  [Due Diligence, 14 days]
      │  AI analysis + technical review
      │  + legal review
      │
  [Commerce DAO Vote, 5 days]
      │
      ├── Approved
      │       │
      │   [Formation]
      │       │  Formation of SIC(p) and AG(p)
      │       │  Issuance of project tokens
      │       │  LP Burn: 0.1% of budget → GBR burn
      │       │
      │   [Accumulation]
      │       │  Collection of investments from SIC(p)
      │       │  Achievement of CC(p) ≥ C(p)
      │       │
      │   [Implementation]
      │       │  AG(p) works
      │       │  Milestone reports every 30 days
      │       │  SIC(p) votes for each tranche
      │       │
      │   [Operation]
      │       │  Project generates revenue
      │       │  Profit distribution:
      │       │    60% — SIC(p) investors
      │       │    25% — AG(p) executors
      │       │    10% — Governance Pool
      │       │     5% — AiC fund
      │       │
      │   [Completion / Continuation]
      │       Final report or transition
      │       to permanent operation
      │
      └── Rejected → [Archive] or rework
```

**Examples of typical Commerce DAO projects:**

- **LQD (Liquidity Deployer):** Automated deployment of liquidity pools. Budget: ~15,000 GBR. SIC: ~200 participants. AG: 5 developers + 2 analysts. Implementation period: 6 months. Revenue model: 0.1% fee on deployed liquidity.

- **SAPP (Social Application Protocol Platform):** SDK for developers of decentralised applications on top of DSP. Budget: ~50,000 GBR. SIC: ~500 participants. AG: 12 developers + 3 designers. Period: 12 months. Revenue model: application marketplace (5% commission on sales).

- **PowerSwapMeta:** DEX aggregator with meta-transactions. Budget: ~30,000 GBR. SIC: ~300 participants. AG: 8 developers. Period: 9 months. Revenue model: 0.05% of exchange volume.

### 5.4 Economic DAO

#### 5.4.1 Purpose

Economic DAOs represent **a fundamentally new concept for the organisation of public financing, project management, and socio-economic interaction.** They provide for the accumulation of social, financial, and economic resources for the most effective realisation of any relevant public projects — including projects whose scale and ambitions exceed the capacity of traditional financing mechanisms.

#### 5.4.2 Distinction from Commerce DAO

While Commerce DAOs focus on individual commercial projects with defined profit models, Economic DAOs address **systemic economic decisions** affecting the community as a whole:

- Management of the community treasury
- Allocation of resources across multiple projects and initiatives
- Strategic investments in infrastructure, research, and capacity building
- Inter-community economic agreements and partnerships
- Monetary policy of the GBR ecosystem (e.g., decisions on staking parameters, liquidity provision, token burning)
- Long-term economic planning and resource allocation

#### 5.4.3 Characteristics

- **Highest economic stakes:** Economic DAO decisions affect the economic position and long-term viability of the entire community. Governance processes are the most stringent in the taxonomy.
- **Supermajority requirement:** The most important Economic DAO decisions may require approval by a qualified majority (e.g., 67% or 75%) to ensure broad consensus before disposing of community resources.
- **Extended discussion periods:** Proposals in Economic DAO are subject to extended discussion periods, allowing thorough analysis and debate before voting commences.
- **Expert input:** Economic DAO governance may include advisory mechanisms — expert analysis, simulation results, review of historical precedents — to inform the decision-making process, while preserving the principle that final decisions are made by the community through voting.
- **Systemic risk management:** Economic DAOs are responsible for monitoring and managing systemic risks to the community economy — excessive concentration in specific projects, liquidity risks, dependence on specific external systems, and other threats to the economic health of the ecosystem.
- **AI Treasury Advisor (from A8):** Economic DAO uses an AI agent to inform economic decisions:

```
AI Treasury Advisor (AiC implementation, Circuit 1):

  On-chain Analytics Agent:
    — Real-time monitoring of economic flows:
      LP positions, trading volumes, TVL,
      token distribution, concentration
    — Visualisation: integration with Dune Analytics

  Risk Assessment:
    — Systemic risk assessment:
      Risk(ecosystem) = f(concentration, liquidity,
                          correlation, external_deps)
    — Early warning when approaching
      critical thresholds

  Simulation Engine (cadCAD):
    — Modelling the consequences of economic
      proposals before voting:
      "if 5% of treasury is burned → impact
       on liquidity, GBR price, TVL"
    — Monte Carlo simulation on GyberComputer

  AI Treasury Advisor informs, does not decide:
  all analysis results are published as
  a supplement to the proposal in Economic DAO;
  the final decision rests with the participants
```

#### 5.4.4 Formal Governance Parameters

```
Economic DAO Parameters:

  Quorum: 25% of the total number of active participants
  with status ≥ LeadDev

  Discussion period: 14 days (mandatory,
  cannot be shortened)
  Voting period: 7 days
  Approval threshold:
    — Standard economic decisions: >67%
    — Changes to monetary policy: >75%
    — Changes to axioms or architecture: >80%
      + confirmation by MacroeconomicDAO

  Proposal rights:
    — Participants with status ≥ LeadDev
    — Minimum staking: 10,000 GBR
    — Required: economic justification,
      cadCAD simulation (≥1000 scenarios),
      DUNA legal expert opinion

  Voting rights:
    — Participants with status ≥ Dev
    — Weight: Hybrid Voting Power × 1.5 for
      statuses LeadDev and above (expertise premium)

  cadCAD obligation:
    — Every proposal in Economic DAO
      is accompanied by a cadCAD simulation:
      (1) baseline scenario (current parameters)
      (2) proposed scenario (proposed changes)
      (3) stress scenarios (extreme conditions)
    — Results are published as an annex
      to the proposal
    — If the difference between baseline and proposed
      exceeds 20% on key metrics →
      mandatory extended discussion period (21 days)

  Veto mechanism:
    — Core participants (Core status) possess
      the right of suspensive veto
      on Economic DAO decisions for 14 days
    — The veto is not absolute: a repeated
      vote with a threshold of >80% overrides the veto
    — The veto exists as protection against hasty decisions,
      not as an instrument of Core power over the community
```

#### 5.4.5 Types of Economic Decisions

Economic DAO operates in several fundamentally distinct domains, each requiring specific parameters and expertise:

**Type 1: Monetary policy (tokenomics parameters).**
- Modification of the reward rate in UnitManager
- Adjustment of Activity Score thresholds
- Modification of the Halving schedule
- Management of Buyback & Burn parameters
- *Quorum:* elevated (30%). *Threshold:* 75%. *cadCAD:* mandatory

**Type 2: Treasury management.**
- Allocation of Governance Pool funds across directions
- Strategic investment decisions
- Formation of a stabilisation fund
- Management of DUNA Treasury (fiat portion)
- *Quorum:* standard (25%). *Threshold:* 67%

**Type 3: Inter-project coordination.**
- Prioritisation of ecosystem projects
- Allocation of GyberComputer computational resources
- Resolution of resource conflicts between Commerce DAO projects
- *Quorum:* standard (25%). *Threshold:* >50% (simple majority is sufficient for coordination decisions)

**Type 4: System architecture.**
- Modification of DAO class parameters (quorums, thresholds)
- Addition of new DAO classes
- Modification of the Hybrid Voting Power formula
- Modification of the MemberStatus hierarchy
- *Quorum:* elevated (30%). *Threshold:* 80%. *Required:* MacroeconomicDAO confirmation

**Type 5: External relations.**
- Partnerships with other DAO ecosystems
- Cross-chain integration decisions
- Interaction with regulators via DUNA
- *Quorum:* standard (25%). *Threshold:* 67%

#### 5.4.6 MacroeconomicDAO as Meta-Governance

**MacroeconomicDAO** functions as a meta-governance layer coordinating the activities of the four DAO classes. It is the institutional expression of the community's collective economic intelligence — the mechanism through which the community exercises conscious, purposeful governance of its own socio-economic system.

MacroeconomicDAO is not a centralised authority overriding the decisions of individual DAOs. Rather, it is a governance space in which inter-class issues are resolved, the allocation of resources across DAO classes is coordinated, and the general trajectory of the experiment is directed by the collective will of active participants.

**AI augmentation of DAO governance (from A8).** To counteract voter fatigue and cognitive overload as the community scales, all four DAO classes utilise AiC AI services:

- **AI proposal summariser:** For each proposal, a structured summary is generated — the essence, risks, economic consequences, and arguments for and against. Participants receive an objective overview before voting, which supplements rather than replaces discussion.
- **Consequence simulator:** Before voting on economically significant proposals, the results of modelling are shown: impact on the treasury, liquidity, GyberComputer load, and SES parameters. Implemented via cadCAD on GyberComputer.
- **AI discussion summariser:** Automatic summaries of discussions with the main arguments of each side — for participants who cannot follow the discussion in real time. This lowers the barrier to informed participation (A6).

### 5.5 DAO Interaction and Conflict Resolution

The four DAO classes are not isolated from one another. Decisions in one class frequently have consequences for others:

- A Code DAO decision to adopt a new technical architecture may have economic consequences (costs, performance, scalability) requiring Economic DAO consideration
- A Commerce DAO project may require social coordination (community engagement, marketing) falling within the competence of Social DAO
- An Economic DAO resource allocation decision may affect the priorities of Commerce DAO projects

When inter-class conflicts arise, resolution follows a structured escalation process:

1. **Informal coordination:** Representatives of the affected DAOs discuss the matter in shared communication spaces, seeking consensus.
2. **Joint proposal:** If informal coordination produces a resolution, it is formalised as a joint proposal submitted for ratification to the relevant DAOs.
3. **MacroeconomicDAO arbitration:** If informal coordination fails, the matter is escalated to MacroeconomicDAO for system-wide discussion and resolution.

```
Inter-class interaction model:

  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │          MacroeconomicDAO                    │
  │      (meta-governance, arbitration)          │
  └──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘
                     │
        ┌────────────┼────────────┐
        │            │            │
  ┌─────▼─────┐ ┌───▼────┐ ┌────▼──────┐
  │  Social   │ │  Code  │ │ Commerce  │
  │   DAO     │◄┤  DAO   ├►│   DAO     │
  │           │ │        │ │           │
  └─────┬─────┘ └───┬────┘ └────┬──────┘
        │            │           │
        └────────────┼───────────┘
                     │
              ┌──────▼──────┐
              │  Economic   │
              │    DAO      │
              │ (systemic   │
              │  decisions) │
              └─────────────┘

  Interaction flows:
    Social ↔ Code: technical decisions with social consequences
    Social ↔ Commerce: marketing, engagement, social responsibility
    Code ↔ Commerce: technical implementation of commercial products
    Economic ↔ all: financing, resource allocation, monetary policy
    MacroeconomicDAO → all: arbitration, strategic direction
```

### 5.6 Formal Analysis of the Four-Class DAO System

The four-class DAO taxonomy described in sections 5.1–5.4 constitutes not an arbitrary classification but a formally grounded architecture optimised for different types of collective decisions. In this section we formalise the properties of this system and demonstrate its advantages over monolithic DAOs.

#### 5.6.1. Formal Model of a DAO Class

We define a DAO class as a tuple:

```
D = ⟨Q, V, T, P, E, B⟩

where:
  Q — minimum quorum (share of active participants)
  V — voting function
  T — time parameters (discussion_period, voting_period, timelock_delay)
  P — set of admissible proposal types
  E — escalation function (conditions for referring a decision upward)
  B — budget constraints (maximum size of a single proposal)
```

The four DAO classes form a partially ordered set with respect to the level of economic influence:

```
Social ≤ Code ≤ Commerce ≤ Economic

Formally: influence(D₁) ≤ influence(D₂) ⟹
  Q(D₁) ≤ Q(D₂)          — higher quorum
  ∧ T(D₁) ≤ T(D₂)        — longer periods
  ∧ B(D₁) ≤ B(D₂)        — higher budget thresholds
  ∧ approval(D₁) ≤ approval(D₂)  — higher approval threshold
```

This monotonicity property guarantees that decisions with greater economic influence undergo more rigorous scrutiny: from a simple majority in Social DAO (50%, quorum 5%) to a qualified majority in Economic DAO (67%, quorum 25%).

#### 5.6.2. Theorem on the Reduction of Cognitive Load

**Claim.** The four-class system reduces the cognitive load on a participant compared to a monolithic DAO while maintaining or improving decision quality.

**Proof (sketch).** Let N be the total number of proposals in a given period, N_s, N_c, N_m, N_e the number of proposals in Social, Code, Commerce, and Economic DAO respectively, such that N = N_s + N_c + N_m + N_e.

In a monolithic DAO each participant must evaluate all N proposals. Cognitive load: L_mono = N × complexity_avg.

In the four-class system a participant may focus on 1–2 classes in which they are competent, delegating their vote in the rest. Average cognitive load:

```
L_classified = α × N_focused + β × N_delegated

where α ≈ 1 (full evaluation), β ≈ 0.1 (delegate check)
```

For a typical distribution (N_focused ≈ N/4, N_delegated ≈ 3N/4):

```
L_classified ≈ N/4 + 0.1 × 3N/4 = N/4 + 3N/40 = 13N/40 ≈ 0.325N
```

Thus, L_classified / L_mono ≈ 0.325 — cognitive load is reduced by ~67.5%.

Decision quality does not diminish in the process, because: (a) participants vote on matters in which they are competent, reducing the noise of incompetent votes; (b) delegation concentrates voting power among participants with the relevant expertise; (c) different approval thresholds and quorums are optimised for each type of decision. □

#### 5.6.3. Security Analysis: Attacks on Inter-Class Boundaries

The four-class system introduces a new class of attack absent from monolithic DAOs: **cross-class arbitrage** — exploitation of differences in governance parameters between classes.

**Example of an attack.** An attacker submits a proposal to Social DAO (low quorum 5%, simple majority) disguised as a social initiative but with economic consequences equivalent to an Economic DAO decision. For example: "organise a hackathon with a budget of 500 GBR" — formally Social DAO, but the hackathon includes "prizes" in the form of project tokens that are in effect an investment decision.

**Mitigation.** The escalation function E(D) formalises the conditions under which a proposal must be reclassified:

```
Escalation rules:

  1. Budget threshold: budget(proposal) > B(D) ⟹ escalate(D_next)
  2. Inter-class influence: if proposal D₁ has consequences
     for D₂, and influence(D₂) > influence(D₁), then escalate(D₂)
  3. AI classifier: AiC analyses the text and parameters
     of the proposal, recommending a class with a confidence score
  4. Challenge: any participant with status ≥ Dev may
     initiate reclassification of a proposal
     within the discussion_period
```

The AI Cross-DAO Coordinator (Appendix F) automatically analyses each new proposal and assigns it a recommended class. Where the declared and recommended classes diverge, the proposal is flagged as "requiring reclassification" and referred for manual review.

#### 5.6.4. Evolution of Parameters

The parameters of each DAO class (quorum, periods, thresholds) are not static. They are subject to adaptation through Economic DAO on the basis of empirical data:

```
Adaptive rules:

  Rule 1 (Adaptive Quorum):
    If participation in votes of D over the past 30 days
    < 2 × Q(D), then Q(D) := max(Q(D) × 0.9, Q_min(D))
    Rationale: an excessively high quorum under low turnout
    paralyses governance.

  Rule 2 (Escalation Frequency):
    If >20% of proposals of D₁ are escalated to D₂
    over the past 90 days, then revision of the boundary
    of the admissible type set P(D₁).
    Rationale: frequent escalation indicates
    suboptimal classification.

  Rule 3 (Voting Period):
    If the average turnout in the final 20% of voting_period(D)
    exceeds 50% of total turnout, then voting_period(D)
    may be reduced.
    Rationale: late voters had sufficient time
    but did not require it.
```

All parameter adaptations pass through Economic DAO voting (the class with the highest requirements), ensuring system stability — meta-rules cannot be altered by lightweight votes.

---

## 6. The Applied Ecosystem: From Theory to Implementation

The theoretical constructs set forth in the preceding sections find practical expression in specific software products, protocols, and services that constitute the applied ecosystem of GyberExperiment. Each element of the ecosystem implements one or more principles of the cybersocial economy, and together they form a fully functional environment for decentralised socio-economic interaction.

### 6.1 DSP — GyberSocial Platform (Decentralised Social Platform)

DSP is the central hub of the ecosystem — a decentralised social platform that provides the infrastructure for all forms of participant interaction.

```
DSP Architecture:

  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │              DSP — Layers                     │
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                                              │
  │  User layer:                                 │
  │    — Participant profiles (verification       │
  │      via digital signature)                  │
  │    — News feeds (aggregation                 │
  │      from project spaces)                    │
  │    — Reputation system (integration          │
  │      with UnitManager and G-Plan)            │
  │    — Direct communication (P2P encryption)   │
  │                                              │
  │  Project layer:                              │
  │    — Project spaces (for each                │
  │      IPI-model project)                      │
  │    — Discussion directories                  │
  │    — Voting systems (integration              │
  │      with Governor contracts)                │
  │    — Task tracking (G-Plan)                  │
  │                                              │
  │  Infrastructure layer:                       │
  │    — Distributed storage (IPFS)              │
  │    — Blockchain integration (BSC, Ethereum)  │
  │    — P2P network (libp2p)                    │
  │    — End-to-end encryption                   │
  │                                              │
  │  Technology stack:                           │
  │    — Frontend: React/Next.js, TypeScript     │
  │    — Backend: Node.js, Rust (core modules)   │
  │    — Protocol: ActivityPub-compatible        │
  │    — Storage: IPFS + local cache             │
  │    — Identification: DID (Decentralized      │
  │      Identifiers) + Verifiable Credentials   │
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**AI personalisation with data sovereignty (from A8, A3).**
DSP implements intelligent content personalisation without violating user data sovereignty. Formally:

```
Let u ∈ U be a participant, D(u) their local data
(interaction history, preferences, subscriptions).

The personalisation model M(u) is trained exclusively
on the user's device (on-device inference):

  M(u) : D(u) → R(u),

where R(u) is the personalised content ranking.

Privacy invariant:
  ∀ u ∈ U : D(u) ∩ Server_Storage = ∅

No ecosystem server stores or processes
raw user data. On the server side, only
aggregated, anonymised signals are used
(federated aggregation):

  M_global = FedAvg({∇M(u₁), ∇M(u₂), ..., ∇M(uₙ)})

The global model improves through federated learning
(Flower framework), in which only gradients,
not data, are transmitted from devices.
```

In this respect DSP is fundamentally distinct from Web2 platforms, where personalisation is built on the centralised collection and monetisation of user data. In DSP, personalisation is a tool of the user, not an instrument for extracting value from the user.

DSP differs from traditional social platforms in a principled sense: data belongs to users (Axiom A3), the platform code is open (AGPL-3.0), governance is exercised through Code DAO and Social DAO, and monetisation is based on creating value for participants rather than extracting value from their data.

#### 6.1.1. Identification and Authentication Architecture

The DSP identification system is built on a two-level model that balances usability with cryptographic security:

```
DSP Two-Level Authentication:

  Level 1 — Basic access (password):
    — Registration via email + password
    — Limited functionality: viewing profiles,
      reading forums, basic communication
    — Storage: bcrypt-hashed password
      in encrypted Supabase database
    — Sessions: JWT + Refresh Token (30-day rotation)
    — 2FA: optional TOTP (Google Authenticator)

  Level 2 — Full access (wallet):
    — Binding of a cryptographic wallet
      (MetaMask, WalletConnect, Ledger)
    — Unlocks: DAO voting,
      reward receipt, project creation,
      participation in Commerce DAO
    — Wallet = universal primary key
      (wallet address = primary key across all modules)
    — Session upgrade: signature challenge (EIP-4361)
    — DID: binding of a Decentralized Identifier
      (did:gyber:0x...)

  Relationship between levels:
    — User begins at Level 1
    — Binding a wallet upgrades to Level 2
    — Reverse downgrade is impossible:
      once bound, a wallet remains linked
    — Multiple wallets: a user may bind
      several wallets, but only one
      is primary (used for DAO voting)
```

**Verifiable Credentials (VC):** DSP supports the issuance and verification of Verifiable Credentials to the W3C standard for confirming participant skills, achievements, and statuses. Credentials are stored in the user's wallet (not on a server) and may be presented to any party without disclosing superfluous data (selective disclosure via ZK-proofs). Examples: "Participant completed 10 Code DAO tasks" → VC signed by G-Plan oracle; "MemberStatus: LeadDev" → VC signed by UnitManager.

#### 6.1.2. Communication Protocol

DSP uses a federated communication protocol that provides decentralisation without sacrificing convenience:

```
DSP Protocol Stack:

  Public channels:
    — ActivityPub-compatible protocol
    — Federated architecture: each
      project space = a separate server
    — Cross-project communication:
      user subscribes to channels
      of projects of interest
    — Moderation: automatic (AI filters) +
      social (moderators from Social DAO)

  Private channels:
    — End-to-End encryption (Signal Protocol)
    — Group chats: MLS (Message Layer Security)
    — Keys stored on the user's device
    — Server transmits only encrypted packets

  Project spaces:
    — Dedicated forum for each IPI project
    — Binding to DAO class: Social, Code, Commerce
    — Integration with G-Plan: tasks, milestones, reports
    — Integration with Governor: proposals, votes
    — Automatic archiving of completed projects
      on IPFS

  Notifications:
    — Push notifications about DAO votes,
      G-Plan tasks, messages
    — AI prioritisation: important events
      (votes with a deadline, critical PRs)
      receive elevated priority
    — Configurable filters: by project,
      event type, DAO class
```

#### 6.1.3. Modular Extension Architecture

DSP is designed as a modular platform allowing extension through standardised interfaces:

```
DSP Modular Architecture:

  Core:
    — Identification (DID, wallet)
    — Basic communication (ActivityPub)
    — Profiles and reputation
    — DAO integration (Governor, Timelock)

  Modules (extensions):
    — DSP-Marketplace: marketplace of
      decentralised applications
    — DSP-Analytics: dashboards and analytics
      (integration with Dune Analytics)
    — DSP-Education: educational platform
      (courses, certificates as VC)
    — DSP-Media: decentralised media
      (articles, video, podcasts on IPFS)
    — DSP-AI: AI assistant for ecosystem navigation
      (project recommendations,
      personalised feed)

  Extension standard (SAPP):
    — API: REST + GraphQL + WebSocket
    — Authentication: OAuth 2.0 + DID Auth
    — Publication: SAPP Registry (on-chain)
    — Monetisation: via internal tokens
      or subscriptions
    — Review: Code DAO checks security
      before publication in DSP-Marketplace
```

#### 6.1.4. Comparison of DSP with Existing Platforms

| Characteristic | Facebook/Meta | Twitter/X | Mastodon | Lens Protocol | **DSP** |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Data ownership | Platform | Platform | Server operator | User (on-chain) | **User (DID + IPFS)** |
| Feed algorithm | Closed, optimised for engagement | Closed | Chronological | Open | **AI on-device (A3), federated learning** |
| Moderation | Centralised | Centralised | Server operators | Minimal | **Social DAO + AI filters** |
| Monetisation | Advertising (user data) | Advertising + subscription | Donations | NFT | **Value creation (PMIP, Commerce DAO)** |
| Code | Closed | Closed | Open (AGPL) | Open | **Open (AGPL-3.0)** |
| Governance | Corporate | Unilateral (CEO) | Each server separately | Lens DAO | **Code DAO + Social DAO** |
| Identification | Email/phone | Email/phone | Email | Lens Profile (NFT) | **DID + wallet + VC** |
| Blockchain | None | None | None | Polygon | **BSC → GyberNet** |

### 6.2 GyberNet — Decentralised Network

GyberNet is a dedicated blockchain infrastructure that ensures the transparency and immutability of all ecosystem transactions. Unlike general-purpose public blockchains (Ethereum, BSC), GyberNet is designed as a *specialised* network optimised for the needs of the cybersocial corporation: DAO governance, participant activity verification, IPI project coordination, and enforcement of economic protocols.

#### 6.2.1 Architecture and Functions

```
GyberNet Architecture Layers:

  Layer 1 — Consensus:
    — Modified BFT (Byzantine Fault Tolerant)
    — Reputation-weighted validators:
      validator_weight(v) = stake(v) × reputation_score(v)
    — Finality: 3 seconds (single-slot finality)
    — Throughput: 1000+ TPS (target)
    — Energy efficiency: PoS without PoW mining

  Layer 2 — Execution:
    — EVM-compatible virtual machine
    — Contract languages: Solidity ^0.8.20, Vyper
    — Pre-installed contracts (precompiles):
      Governor, Timelock, UnitManager, GBRVotingWrapper
    — Gas model: subsidised gas for
      DAO votes (from Governance Pool)

  Layer 3 — Storage:
    — Merkle Patricia Trie for state
    — IPFS binding for heavy data
      (documents, media, project artefacts)
    — Pruning strategy: archival data
      moved to IPFS; on-chain retains
      only hashes and metadata

  Layer 4 — Network:
    — libp2p for P2P communication
    — Gossip protocol for transaction propagation
    — DHT (Distributed Hash Table) for node discovery
    — TLS 1.3 for inter-node communication encryption

  Layer 5 — Cross-network:
    — Bridges to BSC (main GBR token network)
    — Bridges to Ethereum (DeFi integration)
    — Bridges to TON, Solana (ecosystem expansion)
    — Standard: IBC-like protocol
      (Inter-Blockchain Communication)
```

#### 6.2.2 Validation Model

GyberNet uses a modified Proof-of-Stake model that integrates the ecosystem's reputation mechanism:

```
Reputation PoS (RPoS):

  Participation in validation:
    — Any participant with status ≥ Dev may
      become a validator
    — Minimum staking: 10,000 GBR
    — Activity Score ≥ 50 (confirmation of
      active participation in the ecosystem)

  Validator weight:
    validator_weight = √(staked_GBR) × (1 + AS/100)
    where AS = participant's Activity Score

    Square root of staking prevents
    domination by large holders.
    Activity Score bonuses active participants.

  Validator rewards:
    — Block reward: 10 GBR/block (decreasing
      according to the halving schedule)
    — Transaction fees: 70% to validator,
      30% to Governance Pool
    — Slashing: 5% of staking for double-signing,
      1% for missing >100 consecutive blocks

  Validator rotation:
    — Active set: up to 100 validators
    — Rotation every 1000 blocks (~50 minutes)
    — Priority: validator_weight + randomness
      (VRF — Verifiable Random Function)
```

#### 6.2.3 Specialised Functions for CSC

**Decentralised Name Resolution (GNS — Gyber Name Service):**
- Registration of human-readable names for participants: `alice.gyber`
- Binding to wallet, DID, DSP profile, and projects
- Governance through Social DAO (registration cost, rules)
- Support for subdomains for projects: `lqd.commerce.gyber`

**On-chain Activity Registry:**
- All activity verifications from G-Plan are recorded on-chain
- Immutable history: Activity Score history for each participant
- Used for the calculation of Hybrid Voting Power and rewards

**DAO Governance Hub:**
- All proposals, votes, and decisions of the four DAO classes are recorded on GyberNet
- Cross-DAO references: decisions of one DAO may reference decisions of another
- Governance analytics: on-chain data for AI Treasury Advisor

#### 6.2.4 Deployment Strategy

```
GyberNet Deployment Phases:

  Phase 0 (current): BSC as main network
    — GBR token deployed on BSC
    — UnitManager on BSC
    — Governor/Timelock on BSC
    — Advantage: ready infrastructure,
      low gas costs, PancakeSwap liquidity

  Phase 1: GyberNet Testnet
    — Deployment of test network
    — Migration of governance contracts
    — Testing of RPoS consensus
    — Parallel operation with BSC

  Phase 2: GyberNet Mainnet (Canary)
    — Launch of main network with limited
      validator set (Core + ArchDev)
    — Bridge BSC ↔ GyberNet: GBR on both networks
    — Governance migrates to GyberNet
    — UnitManager remains on BSC
      (to preserve liquidity)

  Phase 3: Full migration
    — All ecosystem contracts on GyberNet
    — BSC → bridge network for external liquidity
    — Public validation: any participant ≥ Dev
```

### 6.3 GyberComputer — Distributed Computing Network

GyberComputer is a distributed network of computing nodes provided by community members for the execution of resource-intensive tasks: training AI models, rendering, scientific computation.

```
GyberComputer Architecture:

  Participant nodes:
    — Provide computational resources
      (CPU, GPU, RAM, storage)
    — Receive reward in GBR
      proportional to provided resources
    — Verification via Proof-of-Computation

  Task scheduler:
    — Distribution of tasks across nodes
      taking into account available resources
    — Prioritisation based on DAO voting
    — Fault tolerance: duplication
      of critical computations

  Integration with AiC:
    — Provision of GPU capacity for
      model training (Circuit 1)
    — Distributed inference for
      AI services (Circuit 3)
    — Federated learning without transfer
      of raw data

  Technology stack:
    — Orchestration: Kubernetes + custom
      scheduler in Rust
    — Communication: gRPC, Protocol Buffers
    — Containerisation: Docker, WASM
    — Monitoring: Prometheus, Grafana

  AI Compute Orchestrator (from A8):
    — Predictive Scheduling: ML model
      (Reinforcement Learning, PPO/SAC)
      predicts optimal task distribution
      across nodes taking into account latency,
      capacity, and availability
    — Anomaly Detection: early detection
      of node failures via metric analysis
      (Prophet/DeepAR) before computation loss
    — Auto-scaling: predictive scaling
      based on usage patterns —
      resource allocation before peak load
    — Proof-of-Computation Verification:
      AI verifies the correctness of computations,
      critical for federated learning (AiC)
```

### 6.4 G-Plan — Task Management and Activity Verification System

G-Plan is an integrated task management system that simultaneously serves as an activity verification mechanism for participants within the UnitManager system.

```
G-Plan Functions:

  Task management:
    — Creation, assignment, tracking of tasks
      within IPI-model projects
    — Task hierarchy: epics → stories → tasks
    — Binding to project milestones
    — Cross-project dependencies

  AI Task Orchestrator (from A8):
    — Decomposition: AI agent analyses
      IPI-model project specifications
      and proposes task breakdown
      with complexity and dependency assessment
    — Assignment: recommendation of executors
      based on competency profile, current
      workload, and execution history
    — Predictive Analytics: completion deadline
      forecast, early warning
      of delay risks
    — Cross-project Dependency Resolver:
      identification of dependencies between tasks
      of different projects, order optimisation
    — All AI Task Orchestrator recommendations
      are proposals: approval of
      assignments rests with the project lead

  Activity verification:
    — Recording of completed tasks on-chain
    — Task confirmation by participants
      of higher status
    — Generation of activity reports
      for UnitManager
    — Wallet classification algorithm:
      active / inactive

  Integration with reputation system:
    — Task execution quality affects
      reputation weight
    — Reputation affects voting weight
      in Code DAO and Commerce DAO
    — Continuous verification:
      a participant who ceases activity
      loses the right to rewards

  AI task quality verification (from A8):
    — Automatic quality assessment of a completed
      task before forwarding for human confirmation:
      Q(task) = AI_Review(deliverable, spec, context)
      Q ∈ [0, 1], where Q < θ_min → return for revision,
      Q ≥ θ_min → forwarding for review by a participant
      of higher status
    — AI does not replace human confirmation
      but serves as a first filter: reduces the load
      on reviewers and ensures basic quality control
      (compliance with specification, completeness, formatting)
    — Threshold θ_min is determined by Code DAO vote

  Sybil detection and farming protection (from A8):
    — Graph Neural Network analyses the wallet
      interaction graph, detecting clusters
      of coordinated/fake accounts:
      Sybil(wallet_cluster) = GNN(G_interactions)
    — Anomaly detection identifies atypical
      patterns: task wash trading, mass
      creation of identical tasks, suspicious
      confirmation chains
    — Proof of Personhood (ZK cryptography):
      proof of "one person — one account"
      without disclosure of personal data (A3)
    — Sybil analysis results are advisory:
      the final decision on blocking
      is made by Social DAO
```

### 6.5 LQD, SAPP, PowerSwapMeta, Contact — Auxiliary Ecosystem Projects

In addition to the core platform components, the GyberExperiment ecosystem includes a number of applied projects implemented or being implemented through the IPI model:

#### 6.5.1. LQD (Liquidity Deployer)

LQD is an automated platform for the deployment and management of liquidity pools for ecosystem project tokens. LQD is a critical infrastructure component enabling IPI-model projects to transition from the Accumulation phase to the Implementation phase.

```
LQD Architecture:

  Components:
    — Pool Factory: smart contract for creating
      liquidity pools (GBR/project_token,
      project_token/USDT)
    — LP Strategy Engine: algorithm for determining
      optimal pool parameters
      (initial price, depth, fee tier)
    — LP Burn Module: mechanism for burning LP tokens
      as proof-of-commitment upon project initiation
    — LP Lock Manager: temporary locking of LP tokens
      to prevent rug-pull
    — Analytics Dashboard: monitoring of TVL, volumes,
      impermanent losses

  Integrations:
    — DEX: PancakeSwap V3, Uniswap V3 (via bridges)
    — Chainlink: price oracles for determining
      initial parameters
    — Commerce DAO: approval of parameters for large pools

  Deployment parameters (configurable via Commerce DAO):
    — Minimum LP Burn: 0.1% of C(p) in GBR
    — LP Lock period: 180 days (default)
    — Fee tier: 0.3% (standard), 1% (volatile tokens)
    — Initial liquidity: ≥$1,000 (in GBR equivalent)

  Economic model:
    — Fee: 0.1% of each deployment (→ Governance Pool)
    — LP incentivisation: additional GBR rewards for
      liquidity providers in the first 90 days
    — Buyback & Burn: 2% of fee revenue → purchase
      and burn of GBR

  AI integration (AiC Circuit 1):
    — Predictive pricing: AI analyses market data
      and recommends the initial token price
    — Impermanent loss forecasting: warning to LP
      of potential losses under various scenarios
    — Liquidity optimisation: automatic rebalancing
      of positions (Uniswap V3 concentrated liquidity)
```

LQD is the first Commerce DAO project to have completed the full IPI cycle: from idea (proposal for LP deployment automation) through SIC formation (~200 participants), accumulation (~15,000 GBR), implementation (6 months, AG = 5 developers + 2 analysts) to operation. Revenue model: 0.1% fee on deployed liquidity; projected annual revenue at TVL $10M = $10,000 in GBR equivalent.

#### 6.5.2. SAPP (Social Application Protocol Platform)

SAPP is a standardised platform and SDK for the creation of decentralised social applications (dApps) on top of DSP. SAPP implements Axiom A4 (extensibility): any developer may create a DSP extension without permission from a central authority.

```
SAPP Stack:

  SAPP Module = {
    manifest.json:     — module metadata (name, version, author,
                         dependencies, required permissions)
    src/:              — module source code (React + TypeScript)
    api-contract.ts:   — typed API contract
                         (what the module provides to DSP)
    permissions.json:  — requested permissions
                         (user data, network, storage)
    tests/:            — automated tests
    audit.sbt:         — AI audit soulbound token (after passing)
  }

  Publication process:
    1. Developer creates a SAPP module
    2. AI Code Reviewer checks the code (vulnerabilities, compliance)
    3. Code DAO peer review (≥2 approvals from Dev+)
    4. Commerce DAO approves the business model
    5. Publication in SAPP Marketplace
    6. DSP users install the module (opt-in)

  Marketplace:
    — Catalogue of approved SAPP modules
    — Ratings and reviews (verified installations)
    — Three categories: free, freemium, paid
    — Monetisation: developer receives 85% of revenue,
      10% → Governance Pool, 5% → AiC fund
    — Internal application tokens: each SAPP
      may issue its own token via LQD

  Examples of SAPP modules:
    — GyberNotes: decentralised note-taking system
      with encryption (DDP + E2E)
    — GyberPolls: advanced polls with QV/CV mechanisms
    — GyberAnalytics: AI analytics of community activity
    — GyberBounty: bug bounty programme management
    — GyberLearn: educational platform with certificates (VC)
```
