### Appendix C. The Eight Axioms of CyberSocium — Summary

```
A1 — DECENTRALIZATION
  No single node, agent, or group can
  exercise control over the system as a whole.
  Implementation: P2P architecture, multisig,
  distributed storage.

A2 — TRANSPARENCY
  All economic transactions and governance
  decisions are recorded on the blockchain and available
  for verification by any participant.
  Implementation: on-chain governance, AGPL-3.0.

A3 — DATA SOVEREIGNTY
  The user is the sole owner of
  all rights to generated content, metadata,
  and any other types of data.
  Implementation: DID, IPFS, E2E encryption,
  zero-knowledge proofs.

A4 — EXTENSIBILITY
  The system is designed for expansion
  without permission from a central authority.
  Implementation: modular architecture, SAPP,
  open APIs, permissionless participation.

A5 — MERITOCRATIC FAIRNESS
  Reward is proportional to verified
  contribution, not to capital, status, or connections.
  Implementation: UnitManager, G-Plan, reputation
  system, verification of activity.

A6 — INCLUSIVITY
  The entry threshold is minimized to ensure
  the broadest possible participation.
  Implementation: PMIP, multilingual support,
  cross-chain compatibility, free
  basic access.

A7 — SELF-GOVERNANCE
  All rules of the system are established
  and modified by the participants themselves
  through formalized voting mechanisms.
  Implementation: four-class DAO taxonomy,
  Governor contracts, Timelock.

A8 — COGNITIVE AUGMENTATION
  The system employs artificial intelligence
  as a tool for augmenting the collective
  cognitive capacities of participants,
  while preserving human control
  over strategic decisions.
  Implementation: AiC (three circuits), federated
  learning, AI audit, AI summarization,
  human-in-the-loop for all critical decisions.
```

---

### Appendix D. Smart Contract Interface Specification

This appendix describes the key smart contract interfaces of the GyberExperiment architecture. All contracts are written in Solidity ^0.8.20 using the OpenZeppelin library and deployed on BNB Smart Chain (BSC).

#### D.1. UnitManager (GybernatyUnitManager)

Canonical contract: `CONTRACTS/unit-manager-dao/UnitManager.sol`

```solidity
// SPDX-License-Identifier: GPL-3.0
pragma solidity ^0.8.20;

// Patterns: UUPS Proxy + Ownable + ReentrancyGuard + Pausable + EIP-712

enum MemberStatus {
    None,       // 0 — not registered
    Unit,       // 1 — basic participant
    Dev,        // 2 — developer
    LeadDev,    // 3 — lead developer
    ArchDev,    // 4 — architect
    Core        // 5 — core (added in v2)
}

interface IUnitManager {
    // === Registration and statuses ===

    /// @notice Register a new participant with initial Unit status
    /// @param wallet Participant's wallet address
    function registerMember(address wallet) external;

    /// @notice Promote a participant's status
    /// @param wallet Participant's address
    /// @param newStatus New status
    /// @dev Requires two-level approval:
    ///      confirmation by participants 1 and 2 levels above
    function promoteStatus(
        address wallet,
        MemberStatus newStatus
    ) external;

    /// @notice Demote status (degradation for inactivity)
    /// @param wallet Participant's address
    /// @dev Called automatically when Activity Score < threshold
    function degradeStatus(address wallet) external;

    // === Rewards ===

    /// @notice Claim reward for the current period
    /// @dev Checks: status, Activity Score (via G-Plan),
    ///      time since last payout (≥ 30 days)
    function claimReward() external;

    /// @notice Claim a project completion bonus (×5)
    /// @param projectId Identifier of the completed project
    /// @dev Checks: project in Operation status,
    ///      msg.sender ∈ AG(project)
    function claimProjectBonus(uint256 projectId) external;

    // === Activity Scoring ===

    /// @notice Update a participant's Activity Score
    /// @param wallet Participant's address
    /// @param score New Activity Score (0-100)
    /// @param proof EIP-712 signature from the verifier
    /// @dev Verifier = G-Plan oracle or signer
    function updateActivityScore(
        address wallet,
        uint8 score,
        bytes calldata proof
    ) external;

    // === State reads ===

    function getMemberStatus(address wallet)
        external view returns (MemberStatus);
    function getActivityScore(address wallet)
        external view returns (uint8);
    function getRewardAmount(MemberStatus status)
        external view returns (uint256);
    function getLastClaimTime(address wallet)
        external view returns (uint256);

    // === Events ===

    event MemberRegistered(address indexed wallet, MemberStatus status);
    event StatusChanged(address indexed wallet,
        MemberStatus oldStatus, MemberStatus newStatus);
    event RewardClaimed(address indexed wallet,
        uint256 amount, bool isProjectBonus);
    event ActivityScoreUpdated(address indexed wallet, uint8 score);
}
```

**Reward table:**

| Status | Reward/period | Project Bonus (×5) |
|---|---|---|
| Unit | 10,000,000 GBR | 50,000,000 GBR |
| Dev | 100,000,000 GBR | 500,000,000 GBR |
| LeadDev | 1,000,000,000 GBR | 5,000,000,000 GBR |
| ArchDev | 10,000,000,000 GBR | 50,000,000,000 GBR |
| Core | Determined by governance | — |

#### D.2. GBRVotingWrapper (Hybrid Voting Power)

```solidity
interface IGBRVotingWrapper {
    /// @notice Compute Hybrid Voting Power
    /// @param account Address of the voter
    /// @return votingPower Voting power
    /// @dev VP = sqrt(GBR_staked) × ActivityMultiplier × StatusBonus
    function getVotingPower(address account)
        external view returns (uint256 votingPower);

    /// @notice Delegate voting power
    /// @param delegatee Address of the delegate
    function delegate(address delegatee) external;

    /// @notice Stake GBR to participate in governance
    /// @param amount Amount of GBR to stake
    function stake(uint256 amount) external;

    /// @notice Withdraw GBR from stake
    /// @param amount Amount of GBR to withdraw
    /// @dev Timelock: 7 days after withdrawal request
    function unstake(uint256 amount) external;

    // === Activity Multiplier ===
    // score ∈ [0, 30)  → AM = 0.5  (50%)
    // score ∈ [30, 60) → AM = 0.75 (75%)
    // score ∈ [60, 80) → AM = 1.0  (100%)
    // score ∈ [80, 100] → AM = 1.5  (150%)

    // === Status Bonus ===
    // Unit: 1.0, Dev: 1.1, LeadDev: 1.2,
    // ArchDev: 1.3, Core: 1.5
}
```

#### D.3. LPBurnInitiator

```solidity
interface ILPBurnInitiator {
    /// @notice Burn LP tokens to initiate a project
    /// @param lpToken Address of the LP token (CAKE-LP GBR-BNB
    ///                or CAKE-LP GBR-USDT)
    /// @param amount Amount of LP tokens to burn
    /// @param proposalType Type of proposal being initiated
    /// @return initiationId Unique initiation ID
    /// @dev LP tokens are sent to 0x000...dead (irreversible)
    ///      Minimum threshold: minBurnValue (in USD)
    function burnForInitiation(
        address lpToken,
        uint256 amount,
        ProposalType proposalType
    ) external returns (uint256 initiationId);

    /// @notice Check the minimum burn threshold
    function estimateBurnValue(
        address lpToken,
        uint256 amount
    ) external view returns (uint256);

    enum ProposalType {
        Research,       // Research project
        Product,        // Product development
        CriticalVote    // Critical vote
    }

    event LPBurned(address indexed burner,
        uint256 amount, uint256 usdValue,
        ProposalType proposalType, uint256 initiationId);
}
```

#### D.4. Governor and Timelock

Standard OpenZeppelin contracts with customization:

```
Governor: OpenZeppelin Governor + GovernorSettings
  + GovernorCountingSimple + GovernorVotesQuorumFraction
  + GovernorTimelockControl

Customization:
  — getVotes() overridden to use
    IGBRVotingWrapper instead of standard ERC20Votes
  — proposalThreshold() depends on DAO class
  — quorum() depends on DAO class and proposal type

Timelock: OpenZeppelin TimelockController
  — minDelay: 24-72 hours (depends on DAO class)
  — proposers: Governor contract
  — executors: Governor contract + any (auto-execution)
  — admin: Gnosis Safe (pause only)
```

### Appendix E. DUNA Legal Framework: Key Provisions

This appendix contains excerpts from the key provisions of the Association Agreement of Gybernaty DUNA, registered in the state of Wyoming (USA) in accordance with W.S. § 17-32 (Decentralized Unincorporated Nonprofit Associations Act, 2024).

#### E.1. Association Structure

**Legal form:** Decentralized Unincorporated Nonprofit Association (DUNA), state of Wyoming.

**Jurisdiction:** Wyoming W.S. § 17-32 (enacted in 2024 specifically for DAOs).

**Key legal properties:**
- Limited liability of participants for the obligations of the association
- Exclusion of fiduciary duties of members (Notice of Restrictions on Duties)
- Recognition of on-chain voting as a legally binding decision-making mechanism
- The public identifier of the governance smart contract (Governor contract address) is specified at registration
- Compatibility with IRS 501(c)(6) for nonprofit status

#### E.2. Roles and Powers

```
Organizer:
  Role: nominal party / registered agent
  Powers: filing documents at registration
  Restrictions: after registration — no management
    rights or access to assets

Administrator (Ministerial Agent):
  Role: external legal/accounting firm
  Powers:
    — Opening and maintaining fiat bank accounts
    — Signing tax returns
      (Form 8832, 990-N) and liaising with IRS
    — Receiving official notices
    — Executing fiat payments
      approved by vote
    — Maintaining bookkeeping and compliance
  Restrictions:
    — MAY NOT initiate expenditures
      without on-chain voting
    — MAY NOT access the crypto treasury
    — MAY NOT block approved decisions
    — May be instantly replaced
      by a Social DAO vote
  Oversight:
    — AI monitor continuously verifies actions
    — Monthly reporting to the community

Token Holders (Gybernaty Community):
  Powers:
    — Initiating and voting on all proposals
    — Controlling the crypto treasury via Governor + Timelock
    — Appointing and replacing the Administrator
    — Modifying governance parameters
  Restrictions:
    — >25% control → BOI Report (FinCEN)
    — Not formal directors of DUNA
```

#### E.3. Key Articles of the Association Agreement

**Article 1. Purpose and Mission.** Gybernaty DUNA is established to develop and support the ecosystem of decentralized socioeconomic interaction (CyberSocium): financing open-source development, supporting research, providing infrastructure, and coordinating community activities.

**Article 3. Membership.** A member of DUNA is any holder of the GBR token with an active Activity Score. Membership is determined by on-chain state and requires no formal application.

**Article 5. Governance.** All decisions are made through on-chain voting in the Governor contract. The outcome of a vote is legally binding for DUNA, the Administrator, and all participants.

**Article 7. Treasury.** Two-level system: crypto treasury (Timelock) and fiat treasury (Treasury Fiat Account + Operating Fiat Account).

**Article 9. Buyback & Burn.** Buyback & Burn is a protocol liquidity management operation (asset management operation) and is NOT a profit distribution. GBR tokens do NOT confer rights to dividends.

**Article 11. Dissolution.** Assets are not distributed among participants. They are transferred to another nonprofit organization with a similar mission. A qualified majority (≥66%) in the Economic DAO with a quorum of ≥30% is required.

**Article 13. Document Priority.** In case of discrepancy between the Agreement and smart contracts, the Agreement takes legal precedence. The code is brought into conformity through the Code DAO.

**Article 15. Intellectual Property.** Code: AGPL-3.0. Brand "Gybernaty": owned by DUNA. Research: CC-BY-4.0.

#### E.4. Two-Level Treasury: Architecture and Control

One of the key architectural decisions of DUNA is the two-level treasury system, which ensures the separation of on-chain and off-chain financial flows while maintaining unified governance through the DAO.

```
Two-Level Treasury:

  Level 1 — Crypto Treasury (On-Chain Treasury):
    Control: Governor + Timelock smart contracts
    Assets: GBR, stablecoins (USDT, USDC), LP tokens
    Location: Gnosis Safe multisig on BSC
    Budget: ~60% of Governance Pool (6B GBR)
    Operations:
      — Reward payouts via UnitManager
      — Staking rewards
      — Buyback & Burn
      — Financing Code DAO and Commerce DAO projects
    Auditability: fully on-chain; any participant
      can verify balances and transaction history
    Signers: M-of-N (current configuration: 3-of-5)

  Level 2 — Fiat Treasury (Off-Chain Treasury):
    Control: Administrator (external firm),
      acts only upon approval by on-chain vote
    Assets: USD, EUR (bank accounts)
    Location: Bank account in Wyoming
    Budget: formed through crypto→fiat conversion
    Operations:
      — Payment of legal and accounting services
      — Payment of hosting and infrastructure
      — Regulatory payments (filing fees, taxes)
      — Payment of external auditors (smart contracts)
      — Payment of contractor services (per 1099)
    Auditability: monthly Administrator report
      to the community + AI monitoring of discrepancies

  Fiat Expenditure Protocol:
    1. Proposal in Economic DAO: "Spend $X on Y"
    2. Vote: qualified majority (67%),
       quorum 25%
    3. On-chain approval → Timelock (48h)
    4. Administrator receives notification + proof of approval
    5. Administrator executes the fiat payment
    6. Administrator provides confirmation (receipt)
    7. AI monitor verifies compliance:
       amount, recipient, purpose
```

The principal advantage of the two-level architecture is that the crypto treasury is fully controlled by smart contracts and requires no trust in physical persons, while the fiat treasury minimizes trust in the Administrator through procedural constraints and AI monitoring. No single individual has simultaneous access to both treasury levels — this ensures the principle of separation of concerns.

#### E.5. Compliance and Taxation

**DUNA's tax status.** Gybernaty DUNA files for 501(c)(6) status (business league) with the IRS. This status provides exemption from federal income tax, provided that revenues are reinvested in the activities of the association and not distributed among participants. Buyback & Burn is classified as an asset management operation, not as a distribution.

**DUNA obligations:**
- Annual filing of Form 990-N (e-Postcard) or Form 990-EZ with the IRS
- Beneficial Ownership Information (BOI) Report with FinCEN if participants with >25% control are present
- Annual Report with the state of Wyoming
- Maintenance of bookkeeping records (GAAP or Cash Basis) through the Administrator
- AML/KYC: not required for on-chain operations; required for fiat operations through a bank

**International participants.** Participants from outside the United States are subject to the tax laws of their own jurisdiction. GBR rewards are classified as income at fair market value at the time of receipt. DUNA does not withhold taxes for non-US participants; responsibility for tax reporting rests with the participant. For participants from EU jurisdictions, consultation with a tax advisor is recommended, given variations in the application of MiCA (Markets in Crypto-Assets Regulation) across countries.

#### E.6. Comparison of DUNA with Alternative Legal Forms

| Parameter | DUNA (Wyoming) | Cayman Foundation | Swiss Verein | Marshall Islands DAO LLC | BVI Ltd |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Jurisdiction | USA (Wyoming) | Cayman Islands | Switzerland | Marshall Islands | British Virgin Islands |
| DAO recognition | Yes (W.S. § 17-32) | No (common law) | No (common law) | Yes (DAO Act 2022) | No |
| On-chain voting | Legally binding | Undefined | Undefined | Legally binding | Undefined |
| Limited liability | Yes | Yes | Partial | Yes | Yes |
| Nonprofit compatibility | 501(c)(6) | No | Limited | No | No |
| Bank accounts | Available (Wyoming banks) | Difficult | Available | Extremely difficult | Difficult |
| Taxation | 0% federal (under 501c6) | 0% (tax haven) | Cantonal tax | 0% | 0% |
| Reputational risks | Low (US jurisdiction) | High (offshore) | Low | High (association with shell companies) | High |
| Registration cost | ~$200 | ~$5,000–15,000 | ~$3,000–10,000 | ~$5,000 | ~$3,000–8,000 |
| Annual maintenance | ~$500 | ~$5,000–15,000 | ~$2,000–5,000 | ~$3,000–5,000 | ~$3,000–5,000 |

DUNA represents the optimal choice for GyberExperiment across a combination of factors: legal recognition of DAO mechanisms, compatibility with nonprofit status, accessibility of banking services, low cost, and minimal reputational risks. The primary limitation is single-state jurisdiction, which requires additional work to ensure cross-jurisdictional compatibility.

### Appendix F. Technical Specification of AI Integration

#### F.1. AI Agent Architecture

```
Multi-agent AiC system (Circuit 1):

  Orchestrator: CrewAI / Microsoft AutoGen
  Models: open-source LLMs on GyberComputer
    — Primary: Llama 3 (70B) or Mixtral (8x22B)
    — Fallback: Llama 3 (8B) for edge tasks
    — Specialized: fine-tuned models for
      specific tasks (audit, moderation)

  Agents:

  1. AI Proposal Summarizer
     Input: proposal text + context
     Output: {essence, risks, economic_consequences,
       arguments_for, arguments_against}
     Deployment: GyberComputer
     Trigger: new proposal in Governor contract

  2. AI Code Reviewer
     Input: PR diff + context
     Output: {vulnerabilities, warnings,
       code_quality, recommendations}
     Integration: GitHub Actions CI/CD
     Tools: Octane Security, Sherlock AI,
       AuditAgent (Nethermind), Slither, Mythril

  3. AI Activity Verifier
     Input: on-chain data + G-Plan + GitHub
     Output: Activity Score (0-100) +
       EIP-712 signature for UnitManager
     Frequency: daily update

  4. AI Treasury Advisor
     Input: on-chain analytics + market
     Output: risk + simulations + recommendations
     Tools: cadCAD, Dune Analytics,
       Chainlink price feeds

  5. AI Moderator (DSP)
     Input: message + Social DAO rules
     Output: {ok, review, reject} + explanation
     Deployment: edge (on-device) for
       privacy + GyberComputer for
       complex cases

  6. AI Cross-DAO Coordinator
     Input: multi-DAO proposal
     Output: routing + impact_assessment
```

#### F.2. Federated Learning

```
Framework: Flower 1.x (flower.ai)
Aggregation protocol: FedAvg + PearFL (adaptive)

Communication:
  — gRPC between nodes and aggregator
  — TLS 1.3 for encryption
  — Differential Privacy: ε = 1.0, δ = 10⁻⁵

Incentivization:
  — GBR reward per training round
  — On-chain recording of rounds in GyberNet
  — Slashing for poisoning attacks

Tasks:
  — LLM fine-tuning (LoRA/QLoRA)
  — GNN training for Sybil detection
  — Recommendation models for DSP
  — CV for content moderation

Node hardware requirements:
  Minimum: 16GB RAM, GPU 8GB VRAM (RTX 3060+)
  Recommended: 32GB RAM, GPU 24GB VRAM (RTX 4090)
  Cluster: A100/H100 (financed by Economic DAO)
```

#### F.3. Sybil Detection: GNN

```
Graph:
  Nodes: wallets (BSC addresses)
  Edges: transactions, project participation,
    votes, DSP interactions
  Features: Activity Score, MemberStatus,
    registration time, transaction volume

Model:
  Architecture: GraphSAGE + attention
  Framework: PyTorch Geometric
  Training: semi-supervised
  Inference: daily on GyberComputer

Metrics:
  Precision ≥ 0.95 (minimizing false positives)
  Recall ≥ 0.85

Integration:
  Sybil flag → AM = 0 → neutralization of voting power
  Challenge via Social DAO (human-in-the-loop)
```

#### F.4. cadCAD Ecosystem Model

```
Agents:
  — Participants: N ∈ [100, 1,000,000]
  — Projects: M ∈ [1, 10,000] with IPI cycle
  — AI agents: K ∈ [1, 100]

State space:
  — GBR_supply(t), GBR_price(t), TVL(t)
  — N_active(t), M_projects(t)
  — treasury_balance(t)

Governed parameters:
  — staking_reward_rate, burn_rate
  — quorum_threshold, voting_period
  — lp_burn_minimum, activity_threshold

Stress scenarios:
  — 10× participant growth over 6 months
  — GBR_price crash → 0.1× over 1 week
  — Coordinated Sybil attack (1,000 accounts)
  — Exit of 30% of Core/ArchDev participants
  — Regulatory ban in a major jurisdiction

Health metric:
  Health(t) = w₁·liquidity + w₂·participation
    + w₃·project_success_rate + w₄·treasury_runway
```

#### F.5. AI Governance: AI Resource Management Protocol

Governance of AI components in a decentralized system raises unique challenges absent from traditional organizations: who decides which data are used for training? who controls fine-tuning? how is an audit trail ensured for AI decisions? This section specifies the AI Governance protocol, implementing the principle "AI is subordinate to the DAO, not the reverse."

```
AI Governance Protocol:

  Level 1: Model Configuration
  ──────────────────────────────────
    Decides: Code DAO (simple majority)
    Scope: choice of base model (Llama/Mixtral/etc.),
      framework versions (Flower, PyTorch),
      inference parameters (temperature, top_p)
    Timelock: 24 hours
    Rationale: technical decisions, reversible,
      low risk impact

  Level 2: Training Policy
  ──────────────────────────────────
    Decides: Social DAO + Code DAO (cross-class;
      both classes must approve)
    Scope: which data are permissible for training,
      Differential Privacy parameters (ε, δ),
      fairness constraints, content policies
    Timelock: 48 hours
    Rationale: affects participant privacy
      (A3) and social norms (A6)

  Level 3: Deployment
  ──────────────────────────────────
    Decides: MacroeconomicDAO (qualified
      majority 67%)
    Scope: deployment of a new AI agent,
      removal of an existing agent, modification of AI
      access rights to on-chain operations
    Timelock: 72 hours
    Rationale: AI with on-chain rights can
      execute financial operations; maximum
      caution is required

  Level 4: Kill Switch
  ──────────────────────────────────
    Decides: Emergency multisig (Core + ArchDev, 3-of-5)
    Scope: immediate shutdown of any AI agent
    Timelock: 0 (instant execution)
    Post-hoc: Emergency Proposal in Social DAO
      within 24 hours for ratification
    Rationale: protection against compromised AI, hallucination
      with financial consequences, data breach
```

Every consequential action of an AI agent (Activity Score assignment, Sybil flag, treasury recommendation) is recorded in an on-chain audit log through the specialized AiCAuditRegistry contract:

```solidity
// AiCAuditRegistry pseudocode
interface IAiCAuditRegistry {
    event AiAction(
        uint256 indexed actionId,
        address indexed aiAgent,
        bytes32 actionType,     // SCORE_UPDATE, SYBIL_FLAG, etc.
        bytes32 inputHash,      // SHA-256 hash of input data
        bytes32 outputHash,     // SHA-256 hash of output
        bytes32 modelHash,      // hash of model weights
        uint256 timestamp
    );

    // Any participant can challenge an AI action
    function challengeAction(
        uint256 actionId,
        string calldata reason
    ) external;

    // A challenge routes the action to Social DAO
    // for human review
}
```

This mechanism ensures *transparent AI accountability*: every AI decision has a cryptographically verifiable audit trail (which model, on which data, what result), and every decision can be challenged by a participant through the DAO. AI in CyberSocium is not a "black box" but a *verifiable instrument* subordinate to collective governance.

#### F.6. AI Model Update Protocol

Updating models in production is one of the highest-risk operations in AI systems. In centralized organizations a model is updated by decision of the ML team; in CyberSocium — by decision of the DAO, with safety guarantees.

```
Model Update Protocol (MU):

  Stage 1: Proposal (Code DAO)
  ──────────────────────────────
    Initiator: any Dev+ participant
    Content: {model_hash, training_report,
      benchmark_results, diff_analysis}
    Requirement: benchmark on standard dataset
      ≥ baseline (current model) on all metrics

  Stage 2: Shadow Testing (7 days)
  ──────────────────────────────
    New model runs in parallel with the current one
    Results of both are recorded, but only
    the current model affects the system
    Metrics: accuracy, latency, fairness_score,
      resource_consumption
    Automatic rejection if:
      — accuracy < baseline - 2%
      — latency > baseline × 1.5
      — fairness_score < baseline - 5%

  Stage 3: Canary Deployment (7 days)
  ──────────────────────────────
    5% of requests processed by the new model
    Monitoring: anomaly detection on outputs
    Automatic rollback if:
      — anomaly rate > 3%
      — user complaints > threshold
      — resource consumption > budget × 1.2

  Stage 4: Gradual Rollout (14 days)
  ──────────────────────────────
    5% → 25% → 50% → 100%
    At each stage: 48 hours of monitoring
    DAO vote for the 50% → 100% transition

  Stage 5: Decommission Old Model (7 days)
  ──────────────────────────────
    Old model remains available as fallback
    after 7 days — archiving
    Full cycle: ~5 weeks
```

This protocol ensures a balance between innovation (regular model updates) and stability (multi-layered protection against regressions). The key difference from industry practice: the decision on final deployment (50% → 100%) is made by the DAO, not the ML team.

#### F.7. Ethical Constraints on AI in the CyberSocium Ecosystem

The AiC AI components operate under a set of formal constraints derived from the axioms of CyberSocium:

**Constraint 1: Prohibition on autonomous financial operations.** No AI agent may independently initiate a GBR transfer, a modification of staking parameters, or an LP Burn. AI may *recommend* (Treasury Advisor), but *execution* always requires DAO voting or multisig confirmation. Rationale: A7 (self-governance) means governance *by people*, not by algorithms.

**Constraint 2: Transparency of training data.** For each model deployed in AiC, the following is published: (a) a description of the training dataset (without disclosure of private data); (b) the training method (architecture, hyperparameters, number of epochs); (c) fairness metrics across protected groups (jurisdiction, MemberStatus, duration of participation). Rationale: A2 (transparency) extends to AI components.

**Constraint 3: Right to Human Review.** Any participant affected by an AI agent decision (Activity Score, Sybil flag, content moderation) has the right to have the decision reviewed by a human. A review request is submitted to the Social DAO and considered within 72 hours. The AI decision is suspended until the review is completed. Rationale: A5 (meritocratic fairness) requires the ability to correct errors; A6 (inclusivity) prohibits discrimination on the basis of algorithmic bias.

**Constraint 4: Prohibition on profiling for influence.** AiC AI models may not be used to create personalized "nudge" mechanisms directed at altering participants' voting behavior. The AI Summarizer provides *the same* information to *all* participants; personalization is permitted only for UX (language, display preferences), not for the content of governance materials. Rationale: A1 (decentralization) is incompatible with algorithmic manipulation of governance; A3 (data sovereignty) prohibits the use of behavioral data for influence.

**Constraint 5: Graceful degradation.** The system is designed to function *without* AI components — with degraded performance but without loss of functionality. If all AI agents are unavailable: Activity Score is computed by a simplified formula (on-chain metrics, without AI verification); Sybil detection switches to manual mode (Social DAO monitoring); DAO proposals are submitted without AI summarization (participants read the full text). Rationale: A4 (extensibility) means that AI is an *extension*, not a *dependency*; the system must be robust to the failure of any component.

### Appendix J. Map of Theoretical Dependencies

This appendix visualizes the logical structure of CyberSocium theory — the dependencies between axioms, mechanisms, theorems, and technical components. This map enables the reader to: (a) trace the logical chain from each axiom to a specific technical implementation; (b) identify which components are required for each theoretical result; (c) assess the impact of each individual decision on the system as a whole.

#### J.1. Axioms → Mechanisms → Technical Components

```
Dependency graph (simplified):

  AXIOMS                  MECHANISMS                 TECHNOLOGY
  ══════                  ══════════                 ══════════

  A1 (Decentralization) ─→ PMIP                   ─→ UnitManager
                        ─→ Four-class DAO          ─→ Governor × 4
                        ─→ Progressive Decentr.    ─→ Timelock + Gnosis Safe

  A2 (Transparency)     ─→ Open-source (AGPL)     ─→ GitHub repos
                        ─→ On-chain audit trail    ─→ BSC/GyberNet explorer
                        ─→ Public cadCAD           ─→ cadCAD simulations

  A3 (Data             ─→ Federated Learning      ─→ Flower + PySyft
      Sovereignty)     ─→ Client-side encryption  ─→ DDP (IPFS + ACL)
                        ─→ DID/VC                  ─→ W3C standards

  A4 (Extensibility)   ─→ UUPS Proxy pattern      ─→ Upgradeable contracts
                        ─→ SAPP modules            ─→ DSP plugin system
                        ─→ Modular degradation     ─→ Microservices arch.

  A5 (Merit. fairness) ─→ Hybrid VP               ─→ GBRVotingWrapper
                        ─→ MemberStatus hierarchy  ─→ UnitManager.setStatus()
                        ─→ Activity Score          ─→ G-Plan + AI Verifier

  A6 (Inclusivity)     ─→ PMIP (cost → 0)         ─→ Low gas (BSC)
                        ─→ Low barrier entry       ─→ Wallet = PK
                        ─→ Accessibility (WCAG)    ─→ DSP Client UX

  A7 (Self-governance) ─→ MacroeconomicDAO         ─→ Cross-DAO Coordinator
                        ─→ FRP                      ─→ Fork Protocol contracts
                        ─→ SES                      ─→ Replicator dynamics

  A8 (Cognitive        ─→ AiC (3 circuits)         ─→ AI agent pipeline
      augmentation)    ─→ AI Summarizer             ─→ LLM (Llama/Mixtral)
                        ─→ GNN Sybil detector       ─→ PyTorch Geometric
                        ─→ AI audit                 ─→ Slither + Mythril
```

#### J.2. Theorems and Their Dependencies

```
Proof structure:

  Theorem 1 (Universal Realizability of PMIP)
    Depends on: definition of PMIP, NFC, SIC, SR(p)
    Used in: justification of A1, A6; comparative analysis (7.5)
    Technical implementation: UnitManager reward distribution

  Theorem 2 (Scale Inversion)
    Depends on: Theorem 1, definition of individual_cost
    Used in: the "millions = billions" argument (3.4.3)
    Technical implementation: SIC formation incentives

  Theorem 3 (Antifragility of PMIP)
    Depends on: Theorem 1, definition of NFC, external shocks
    Used in: justification of CSC resilience (3.6.4)
    Technical implementation: Fund Monitoring + Halving

  Theorem 4 (O(n) coordination complexity with AI)
    Depends on: A8 (cognitive augmentation), definition of AiC
    Used in: justification of DAO scalability (4.8)
    Technical implementation: AI Summarizer + AI Cross-DAO Coordinator

  Theorem 5 (Reduction of cognitive load)
    Depends on: four-class taxonomy, definition of L(t)
    Used in: justification of DAO differentiation (5.6.2)
    Technical implementation: Governor × 4 with different parameters

  Theorem 6 (Incentive compatibility of SES)
    Depends on: definition of M_SES, Activity Score, Hybrid VP
    Used in: justification of CSC mechanism design (3.5.7)
    Technical implementation: GBRVotingWrapper + UnitManager

  Theorem 7 (Stability of multi-population SES)
    Depends on: Theorem 6, four-class taxonomy
    Used in: justification of the ecological model (3.5.8)
    Technical implementation: Four DAO treasuries + MacroeconomicDAO
```

#### J.3. Critical Implementation Path

Based on the dependency graph, the critical path is identified — the minimal sequence of implementations required for the MVP to function:

```
MVP Critical Path:

  1. GBR Token (BEP-20 on BSC)               — tokenomics foundation
       ↓
  2. UnitManager v2 (MemberStatus 6)          — statuses + rewards
       ↓
  3. GBRVotingWrapper (Hybrid VP)             — voting
       ↓
  4. Governor × 4 + Timelock                  — four DAO classes
       ↓
  5. DSP Client (wallet + governance UI)      — user interface
       ↓
  6. GPROD (blockchain middleware)            — link between UI and blockchain
       ↓
  7. G-Plan v1 (task management)             — Activity Score
       ↓
  8. DUNA registration (Wyoming)             — legal status

  All components (1)–(8) are blocking: without any one of them
  the MVP does not function. The order is determined by technical dependencies.
  Expected time: Phase I (2024–2025).
```

This dependency map is a working tool for developers and researchers within the ecosystem. It will be updated as the theory and implementation evolve — every change in the axiomatic system or architecture is traceable through the dependency graph to all affected components.
